Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse," and it is that you make behind the patient who has this illness to shave the hair from his forehead; then you make three incisions on the forehead equally according to its length; and let one of these incisions be as two thumbs apart in the middle of the forehead going down until the nose, and the other two at each side over the temples, and take care not to cut into the arteries that are near both sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the width of three thumbs across; then prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, and place the spatumile sharp on both sides as this is its form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts to the surface of the skin over the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then withdraw this sharp instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first groove the instrument called "cultellaire", which is very well suited for cutting on one side, and smooth on the other side, not cutting:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh of the chest, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to those near the chest, and then make another incision in the middle groove to the other side; and then draw out blood evenly, and apply pressure to stop bleeding; then place a pad of old cotton in each groove, cover with cloths soaked in wine and oil and pitch, and guard against abscesses from forming; on the third day loosen the bandage, and administer plenty of cold water, then treat it with ointment basilicon mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the phlegm of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When phlegm comes to someone frequently, and you see the eyes swollen and small, with weakened vision, and the whites burned; and hair falls out, and in the head there is pain from a cold, and the patient sneezes; then you know by these symptoms that those matters and that catarrahal condition do not come except from many veins, and if this nasal discharge exists, it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lie with their back against their forehead, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another on the side of the head.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision on the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go until it reaches the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the incision and place old cotton in it, and cover with linen strips; then bind on moist cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful of hot abscesses; when they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow back, then treat it with substances that stimulate growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to generate flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, or a mineral stone or similar thing such as iron; seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and saliva and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other substance that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then let a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil be applied, then proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze from powder, and plug their nostrils when they are about to sneeze, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the stone comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then proceed with extraction using fine forceps, which are described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, then proceed with extraction using a fine needle of thin double thread; and if it does not come out by this means, make a silk cord and insert its end into the ear canal firmly, and plug what is around the cord with soft wax so that wind cannot enter through the cord; then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take bird glue and place some instrument suitable for this purpose, and wrap a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot avoid all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear as one would an abscess, and for cramp; the method of cutting is that you first let the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and draw out the blood according to the measure of her strength, then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat or hanging part; and may the cut be as a crescent, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck out quickly with your mouth; and treat her until she is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if the grain is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer this subtle spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And administer an incision of that tumor.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the tumor is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have done many cases; then extract it with fine forceps and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute cases where fluid falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing powder first, and stuff the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that side where the fluid is in the ear.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it comes out because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not that way, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and light, and heat them slightly over fire; and put one stone in the patient's ear, and place another stone on the side opposite their foot; and continue doing this with stone upon stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out; and if you wish, take a reed, and insert one end of it into the ear, and set fire to the other end so that almost all of the softer part is burned; then do likewise with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the creature, if it is small like a flea or similar things, treat as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use forceps for extraction; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, remove them with fine tweezers, and if none are seen, take this cord:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then gradually form it throughout the cord; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, plug around the cord with cotton as I have said about stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that ancient practitioners have tested for worm removal, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, the form of which is shown as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or brass, make it narrow with small holes, and above cover it to drip; and for pressing inside the distillation use a well-made brass instrument, and if you wish take a scraper and wrap around the tip appropriately cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you want of your medicines in the tube, and let the tube be in the ear; then put inside the scraper on all the cotton, and press with your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and the patient feels it within, and keep the distillation a little heated by fire as one distills it into the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to wound obstruction, or flesh growing inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes occur completely within the ear, so that one cannot see them; and at other times it happens that the hole can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that occurs completely inside and cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see a scab clearly visible, then perform this operation using this spatula which has the following form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front while completely flat at the back so that it does not damage the ear; if the scab is flesh grown within or on the ear, hold it with fine forceps and gently scrape away all the flesh.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is in the ear, take a fine sharp instrument and heat it slightly over fire, then place it in the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction causing the patient pain in the ear, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for as many days as it takes for the wound to heal, or take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue treating until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, plunge a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eyelid that comes on papers when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with pliers and clamps, and cut off a piece from the root with a scalpel; then put on the affected area ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not respond to this treatment, use the fire cautery with a lentil-shaped tool and let them heal after incision; and many times they need repair because something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	from the hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come on the eyelids things that seem like hailstones in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is an accumulation of thick moisture in the upper and lower eyelid; the treatment is as follows: observe if the hail moves from side to side, and it is easy to know; then treat it broadly, then lightly peel off each part, then grasp it with clamps, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the membrane, do not cause any harm to the patient; and if the wound is large, then sew it up with stitches, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, make no effort, for the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grain is inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the membrane, and extract the grain with forceps, cutting and pressing on both sides; and if the membrane is pulled away by the incision, it does not harm; and when the grain is removed, lift the eye with salt water, and treat the area that regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the membranes above the eyes, and this happens more to children than to some people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep like that, and their membranes below their eyebrows are moistened which appear covered with exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your thumb and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places his head on your hand; and then take a piece of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, then place it over him; and press with your thumbs from both sides so that the exinach comes together within the circle; then make an incision in the middle with a sharp spatula no wider than the cut made for opening a vein; and cut through the membrane perfectly until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, exinach will come out of the incision, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull it then in one piece of torn cloth between your two fingers to spread it out, and move your hand right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to apply too much pressure at the opening, so that you do not bring all the spatumile up to the eye, so that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not open at the beginning of the opening, gradually enlarge the opening slightly until it opens; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them on the spot, and pull it out in layers.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of an abscess becoming hot, then treat with poultices soothing until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the eyeslashes
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow around the eyes in a manner not natural and become irritated, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and inflammation of the eyelids and conjunctiva, to the point where it is the cause of eye destruction; and the treatment follows four methods: either by cautery with fire together, or by medicine according to what was mentioned before in the chapter on cautery, and it can be done either by incision and suturing or by cains (a type of needle), as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, put a needle along all the thread; and let this be near the margin of the paper where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread above the entire paper, and turn to the razor; then cut in the part below the paper, below the adjacent hairs, across the spatumile cutting from the large tear gland to the small; then pull out the thread, and place under the paper a small pad of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper a figure of a shield, like the leaf of myrtle, and in all cases it must be that the figure is according to the quantity you wish to raise the paper which is designated for you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one needs to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened; then cut across both lines that you have marked, and start from the main artery until small; let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert an awl into one of the two corners of the eye, then peel it entirely; then sew together the two lips with a needle and a single thread of fine linen, and wipe away the blood, and reduce the excess threads over both eyebrows using some sticky substances if you wish to do so; and if not, do not worry about it, then leave the stitches and threads until three or four days; then heal the wound without stitching dry and constricting materials because the paper rises suddenly from the wound and assembles itself, but the stitch is clumsy (as the ancients say), and this work can be done without fear; and there is another way: which is to mark the paper with a shape that resembles the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, three inches apart according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which rise above the small forces evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the ability to hold the forceps, and the things are not equal, then take a needle with a thread, and place it in the figure; and put one thread next to the large wound margin, and the second thread next to the small, and join between your two threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described, then close both edges of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; but sometimes the hair on the paper turns: in such cases, you should follow what we have said about incisions; however, the suture on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canthi is according to this form: and that you turn the paper and cut into it as I have said, and then make two canthi by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatulum are; and tie at the two edges where you hold the threads; then assemble one upon the other subtly on what protrudes from the paper of the eye, and pull tight the two canthi from both parts firmly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is tied will die and become blackened and fall off, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut with force, and treat until he is healed; and when the wound is sealed, and if the paper is raised, and the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and place a thin silk thread underneath it; then join the ends of the hair and tie them carefully, with the length of the threads one palm long; then arrange in the wound another thin silk thread briefly, and knot the heads of the thread; then have the patient put their head on your shoulder; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a delicate and small operation, then pierce the needle all through the wound at the root of the hair adjacent to it quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the wound, and place in the wound that hair if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out completely from the wound with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the probe is treated and the hair does not come out with it, pull the probe to the back along all the thread that you have ordered, until the probe comes out of the hole above and you can see it by eye; then pull out the probe and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows over; and if the hair is short, attach one long hair from natural hairs, and raise it with that which you left, until it is lengthened and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pus of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or pus comes in the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is that you should split the wound open, and separate its edges, and place linen strips inside it, and treat it until it heals; and it is not appropriate to use in the care of it things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but use things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and boil water or barley with flax seeds, and apply a poultice made from melted myrrh mixed in some oil, and wrap a dressing around it, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal in a way different from its former state; and all the works we have mentioned are nothing but methods to prevent this disease from returning in a form different from its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and it is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental cause comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, on which there should be double thread, and insert it into the flesh, piercing from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread goes through two points of the flesh; then stretch the flesh over the entire needle, and cover it with a piece about one spatumile wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the crevice, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side of where the paper was; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you made, and make them so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the figure of a letter called "I griesche"; then remove that flesh according to the sharpness of its sides underneath, from what was under the paper, then join the two separated parts with thread; then treat it as we have said concerning softening medicines and bandages until he is well.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a complete incision under the hairs of the paper, and as was said before; then separate between the two sides of a bandage, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in appearance, and wise masters equip themselves with all their power to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary of work and instruments in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must apply the tip of a razor beneath the skin, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut away what is attached to the delicate spatumile, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot endure a sharp spatumile scraping the eye; and your incision, by which you peel off this assembly, must be lightly made, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and all of this assembly is healed, and sometimes it makes the eye watery and salted, and lift it with fresh water and honey; then place between the skin and the eye a piece of linen cloth, and put on the eye wool moistened abundantly in egg whites; and after three days use honey and other soothing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is like frozen white moisture, so when one touches it with iron and thinks to remove it with pincers, one cannot; and both appearances begin near the large tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all of the sight and all of the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then works the eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the nail with pincers gently, and stretch it out; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair on it, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, and pierce it all the way through the nail, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it out, and scrape off all the hair from the side of the nail that is near the tear duct and tie the thread to the root of the eyelash up to the head; then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct using the fine spatula and small forceps, leaving the natural flesh of the tear duct so that by the incision the flow of tears does not habitually come forth; and sometimes they stretch the nail only onto a needle and with thread as we have said; then scrape all the thin layer underneath where this form is:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the speculum does not touch the delicate tissue and break it, and that the probe is not pierced; and after the incision throw into the eye a little ground sulphur and of litharge made into paste, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not attached to the nerve and you cannot insert the needle, and the hook cannot enter, this condition of the nail is often treated with medicines; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, use caution for the patient’s eye, and take a light speculum according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently from above, and if you see that it is diminishing in size and the flesh is closing around it, then drip from your mouth into the eye a paste made of litharge and red precipitate and ground sulphur, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it first, and cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it at the nail, and cut off a part but not all, so that no tears come forth; then let drops fall into the eye of red chyle which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some people's eyes, red flesh occasionally grows and covers the pupil, restraining it behind the eyelids and turning it outward, resembling a purple rose. The treatment is that the patient places their head in a healthy position, then the eye is treated, and all such flesh is coiled with appropriate hooks and held firmly; then cut off the first layer of flesh and continue cutting to the end with scissors, being careful not to injure the eye during this work. Make the incision on the spatumile as we have described in the incision of a nail and small forces from which the sebela is removed, as the forms after this chapter demonstrate; when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, apply to the eye a poultice made from finely ground seeds or other red-coloured medicines that are corrosive, and place over the eye outward cotton with vinegar so it remains free of hot abscesses; if anything remains and a warm sweat rises, and you fear a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the hot abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus you will deal with such flesh that is attached to the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you lighten the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, with iron work; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Blood vessels are red and covered over the eye, and their work endangers vision and weakens the eye all the time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must check if the eye, in which there is a growth, is healthy otherwise, and there is no other disease except for the growth; then treat it as follows: instruct the patient to place his head on your lap, then suspend those vessels along the whole vein according to your knowledge, and let the veins be fine double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two trephines by degrees on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully open those veins with forceps, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move away from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the lancets, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not touch anything other than those veins; and when you have done this, let drops of green and red collyrium fall into the eye to dissolve what remains of the sore.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove all of it at that hour, apply a poultice to the eye with soothing substances for the pain in the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and is assured of a hot abscess, then resume according to this manner as described before until he is healed; and this is the form of the procedure:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I said before, and it is not healed, there is pus inside that you must incise at the abscess, where it should drain, and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then remove it with all the instruments as described here; and it is called "aspre chief," and should be made of iron shaped like a head reont, and should be pointed like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place over the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press gently until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the skin is adhered and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowel is adhered, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, know that he is well; if this is not so, then there is another plan to bring the fistula back to the opening of the navel according to this form: which is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and with hot medicines, and when it has been uncovered take one frame according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and the shaft should be slender up to its end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the lamina, and move your hand from the eye one inch, then turn the frame completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels that wind if he holds his hand over his navel; and then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and hardens the skin, let the matter go to the navel; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the outlet of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no obstruction or reduction in vision, you must bind the patient; then wash it clean, then apply cupping vessels without striking to suck out impurities, then place on the eye a poultice made of acacia, aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and then bandage the eye; and the method for the cloths is that you take soft cloths, and double each in four layers, and then place one over another according to the size needed by the eye; then press it tightly with a hard bandage, and again apply cupping vessels without striking; then remove the cupping vessels and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the poultice becomes soft, you must bind it firmly; then after the day and night have passed, if you see the eye healing well, that is good; if not, then repeat the poultice and cloths and binding and cupping until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the rupture of the eye membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes to the eye membrane, it is opened, and there appears force from the papers like a grain of resin, which is terrifying to see; then if you wish to treat it, you place one needle at the root of the part below up to that above, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the part of the tear duct; and make it pierce, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut the area of the double thread and tie a part of the uvea around it tightly, then remove the needle and put on the eye wool soaked in abundance of egg white; leave it until the threads fall with the uvea, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is restrained by the uvea from all sides with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears very swollen, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes in line with the eye, and let the white fluid drain out and lower the eye; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than fluid gathered in the eye, resembling an inflow of water, but it is not actually water; and the manner of its appearance is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the fluid rise to above your eyes; then if it remains there without descending and obscuring the light, know that it is an inflow of water, and if the descent of the fluid is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Situate the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and cut through the corneous membrane in a small spot along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneous membrane and the corona, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, pour into the eye hot honey mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it further as needed until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	for the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing them; act according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and with the healthy eye tightly pressed; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take in your right hand, if the eye is the left one, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is the right one; then place the tip of the instrument just below the corona by a thickness of a hair at that clear part of the eye near the lesser tear gland, then insert the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it penetrates into the clear part of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches an empty space; and the length of the path of the almagda should be perfectly measured from the diameter of a plum to the end of the blackness; this is the corona of the eye; you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corneous membrane, then place the instrument where the water is, and press it out one path at a time.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows now, let the patient see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, if the water rises again, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and does not rise further, gently turn your hand little by little; then add a small piece of sapphire to the water, and lift the eye from there.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place behind the eye plugs made of wool soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg whites, and secure with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it mixed with egg in abundance.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but act with subtlety, then insert the almond as we have said; and upon completing the work, prepare for the patient a resting place where they may sleep on their back in a dark room; and ensure that all movements are avoided, and give light foods, and do not move their head neither to the right nor left, and bind them according to their disposition until the third day; then unbind them in the same dark room, test their vision, show them some things, and then rebind them until the seventh day; and it is not necessary to perform this during the hour of the cure or immediately after the incision now, but you must delay this because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses form, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who treats abscesses; and when it is appeased, then release the vision and place upon it a single strip to cover for some days, and let it be immediately in a dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house bit by bit, and return to his usual activities; and know that no student should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Irach, who told us that in his country people make small holes for water extraction, but nevertheless I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor have I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new invention.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, for those who do not recognize them; and they are properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the front part of these be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh grows on the nose in various forms, some of which appear like many-footed scorpions; and there are such cases where the flesh protrudes with a reddish hue, and there is flesh smooth with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of that flesh which is smooth and not protruding, you should seat the patient between your hands facing the sun; work on his nostrils, apply the lancet to those parts, and draw them out thinly; then proceed as much as you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula from one side, until you know that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be coped with, then use all the fine instruments gently until nothing remains; and if it does not subside, for abscesses that are deep, cut around as is appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood is still and all the flesh is removed, then apply fresh and cold water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose is pierced and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is sound; and if moisture does not come out as it should, know there is flesh grown onto the bone above, which the instrument cannot cut: then you must insert a thick linen thread, tied with knots about an inch apart; and have the patient place one end of the thread in his nostril to the best of their ability, pulling through smelling until it comes out into the mouth; and often children at school do this similarly, and it is easy for whoever wants to do it; then hold one end that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them apart while carefully loosening the knots on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the new flesh has corrupted the old flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then place a silver chain in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, where oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And whether it is of silver or brass, it should resemble an open lamp, like a chain, and the conduit should be similarly designed; and if you wish, make a closed chain, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose and grows until it becomes visible to the eye; and for this you should cut it at the beginning, remove all flesh from it, then apply the cautery or burning medicine over it. If you delay cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a bad color, and slow in sensation: do not touch it with iron as it may be an embedded abscess, for when you cut it once, much harm comes to the patient; but if the abscess is soft to touch, not of a bad color, and you see that all can be cut away, then empty the patient fearlessly and cut it away, and treat the area with drying and binding substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the skin is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilage works, there is little benefit, except in some men.
