Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid treating it with iron, and those who have swelling due to an artery should also be avoided. For someone suffering from a swollen artery, make an incision above the skin longitudinally; then work around the arteries with hooks, carefully separating the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle beneath it, piercing it through to the other side; tie off the artery using double thread at two points as I have taught you when extracting the two arteries in the temples; puncture the area between the two ties with an intravenous needle so that blood flows out from there and loosen the abscess; then apply a treatment derived from bovine milk until the clot discharges; if the abscess is due to a swollen vein, stain your hand with what you can of the abscess on the skin, then insert the needle beneath the spot where your hand touches, piercing it through; tie off the abscess as I have told you using one part of two ends of the thread; and if you are worried that the thread might tear, add another needle under the entire abscess along the incision made by the first needle, tying both threads in four places; then cut the abscess until excess fluid drains out; then cut away any excess heart tissue but leave what is tied off; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, followed by treatments of tents and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in the artery and vein, abscesses also affect the nerves when they are injured, or due to excessive labor, and similar circumstances.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and at all places where there are joints, and these are severe abscesses, and their color resembles the skin color, and they cause intense pain; and when pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not throughout the body, but rather near the heart; and it moves nowhere, neither forward nor backward, nor up or down, and those that occur in joints should not be cut with an iron tool: perhaps this would lead to contraction; and those that occur on the head or forehead, cut the skin at the sutures.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, grasp it with forceps and cut it at its root; and if it is large, incise it with a lancet, then strip it, remove it, and close the wound by suturing, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large hanging pouches
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It sometimes occurs in the abdomen and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and its root is subtle, and the growths are large; there are both small and very large ones. I saw a person who had two of these on their abdomen that were more similar to fungi than anything else, with no difference, they were white, had fine roots, and were somewhat split, and moisture corroded them quickly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found in one eighteen ounces, and in the other six ounces, and the work in the incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of fine texture; cut it with a broad spatula, and have the cautery by the fire ready.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting there often comes excessive bleeding, and if the blood flows too much, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread and tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the linen thread until you cut the artery, and cut it carefully without any effort; and if the roots are thick, there is fear in cutting them equally, but you can cut half of it well, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of reddish color and poor texture and milk-white.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is a rooted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers shortly after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is fierce
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery on a wound or cut to the surface, and it is on the abdomen and there are some boils present, as happens in other ruptures, whether from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is due to the rupture of the surface and the exit of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the skin, and it is a light matter without pain, and clearly has various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses on both sides it swells up, and then returns, and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and you can clearly feel when you press it with your hand that it does not resist; and if it is due to blood, it becomes apparent through these signs as hard and large abscesses, fixed according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft upon touching, and the work consists in observing whether the appearance indicates arterial or venous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to intestine or pus, you must instruct the patient to hold his breath and lie flat, then incise all around the swelling; then have him lie supine between your hands, then work around the area where you have marked for the entire span of the hand, then extend half of the abscess above to the full length of a large needle; then bind it firmly with strong thread or silk cord without leaving any knots; then work on the extended part of the abscess over the bandage and place your index finger there to find the intestine; if you find it caught in the binding, release it and push the intestine back into the abdomen; if you encounter the bladder, grasp it by the needle and cut off the excess; and if an artery or vein opposes you, proceed gently, then return to your work and take two needles, placing two threads through them, and insert the two needles around where you need to pierce in a cross shape; then extract the abscess in four places over the needles, and if necessary, remove the needles when the area has sufficiently dried and the dead tissue has sloughed off, then treat it as we have said; drain any blood or moisture that is found, then treat the wound appropriately, and seal the site.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the similarities of ulcers and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should avoid treatment with iron; and we say that an ulcer originates in the flesh, and there is great caution in its treatment, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be cut out as with ulcers in the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, and you should remove it entirely when it is in the beginning; but when it is large and old, one must not approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal such cases.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the ulcer is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, you should purge the patient of black bile at times; then make them fast if they have obvious fullness, and prepare the patient properly for the treatment; then apply your poultices around the ulcer, and scrape off all the pus from all sides, removing everything without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely until it stops on its own; press well with your hand or something else in the area; if the bleeding is contrary to cutting an artery or vein, cauterize until the blood is staunched; then treat further as needed until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsy (hydrophysis)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already mentioned in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is formed, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is done by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: it is only for "eclites"; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanitis and yposarchia, because this is a lethal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of hydropsy which is called "eclites" with medicine, and the cure does not help, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides hydropsy, such as constipation and flatulence and similar things; do not touch with iron then, because there is doubt; and if you see that the patient is of strong constitution, and he has no other illness but hydropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, you should act thus: lift the patient straight up in your hands, and have an assistant press the belly by pushing out the water to the lowest part of the back, then take the spatumile according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cuts from two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And pierce it, but do not make the incision so deep that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and should not bleed; then observe if the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: in such a case, you must cut above the navel three fingers wide on the left side; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the navel; and if it is because of mucus, do so on the right, but ensure that the patient does not lie on the incision site so that the superfluous fluids can flow towards this weak spot; then perforate all the skin with the instrument, and draw out your hand to about one inch between the skin and the flesh as when peeling, according to the size of a thumbnail or slightly more; then pierce the flesh until the pus comes out at an open place, which is where the water is, and pull it forth strongly, and insert this instrument whose form is as follows:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and it is made of bronze or light iron, and there are in one part I small holes; and on the side, III holes; and II from another side, and I from another; and the head is shaped like a feather, and this is the form of the incision which the writer makes on the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it now descends upon the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or falls into fainting, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the conditions of the patient's strength signify, and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is now retained by the heart which stops up the hole that is on the surface, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument another day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw a small amount of fluid; do this for some days, and guard against overdoing it so that there remains only a little liquid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water in him, then treat with the cure of burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and let him abstain from drinking; and treat with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	about the stiffness of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that he be pierced throughout the septum very finely according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a fine cloth plug in the opening, and secure it for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the plug, allow him to urinate, and then replace the plug; and perhaps no plug is needed, because the urine that comes forth does not leave the plug closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small should be treated with the cloth of flax as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its place are deformed, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies supine on his back, then place the head of the rod and align it as with the width of a pen feather, so that the aperture fits precisely, as it should; and beware of blood loss which happens often, and if it occurs, stop it with what stops bleeding, and treat the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters appear on the penis, and it is an unpleasant appearance; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must pierce them with a fine lancet, clean and empty all of them, then apply cotton moistened with Egyptian ointment; then treat with diafinicon ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and spreading, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is deep in the flesh, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the part of the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is fixed, treat the part that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all at once, the edges of the ulcer are not sure to heal properly, and blackness and corruption come into the flesh around it and the groin; so you must remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice made of pomegranate peel and vinegar, and continue treating it with other methods until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then treat with the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two conditions simultaneously: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, then it must be that you insert a silver tube into the urethra through which the patient urinates; and when hair appears on the head of the uncircumcised penis due to injury or abscess, then it is necessary for you to burn with a sharp instrument until the ligament is loosened, and free the head of the penis from all sides; and if it is difficult to describe this procedure, then it must be that you use an applicator to apply some heat to the tip of the penis and skin; then carefully separate them, and place a fine linen strip soaked in cold water between them so that it does not become irritated again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a disconnection of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the least harmful to their welfare.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, as they did not practice it in their law, and we have nothing but what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and seniors who performed circumcision around the prepuce, with force, and completely anew; they did this because there are two layers, and by chance one might cut through the outer layer while leaving the inner intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it needs to be cut again, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleansing of the stump there is no certainty about the tip of the member; and in the cleaning of the nail by chance the iron slips, and they run the work incorrectly, and many times they are born such that they do not need cleansing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force to the entire limb of thread, I have found through good experiment, because the force cuts precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut evenly in one single motion; but make sure the thread is tight around the skin. The method of the first procedure should be such that if the child understands, you make him think that you are only tying the thread around the shaft and then you can entertain him in all ways possible; then hold it straight between your hands, and apply the force between your hands or at your feet where the child cannot see, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the shaft and blow onto the wound, raise it up until the head of the shaft is out; then clean thoroughly the accumulated dirt from the wound, tie a double thread around the site, tie below the pocket to another limb; hold it by two days with the second binding at the pouch and index finger, cut between the two limbs, lift the heart of the shaft quickly; let the blood flow drop by drop, for this is most suitable; put powder on top of it and then cover the powder with a feather glued with an egg white diluted in rose water, seasoned with good fresh oil, leave it there until the next day, and treat it with other methods as needed until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the force for cleansing is thus: the two blades should be sharp and even, and the blades as wide as the handle equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing occurs when pus inside flows to the incision; then it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, just as one would an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your fingernail, then hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and the area below the shaft is swollen, then leave it until the abscess is sufficiently abated, and gently scrape it; cut as much as you can move, and be careful of the part of the shaft, so that it does no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the site of a superficial wound with powder, as we have said in the chapter on powders, and if you cut into the chest beyond measure, and it goes too far, it will not harm; treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or congealed blood, or bladder, or dead tissue, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine does not flow, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone lodged at the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be seated on their knees; and place their feet on his back, and extend his belly above the back, and press down on the patient's abdomen as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards, so that the urine becomes free; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe," which has this form: it should be made of fine silver wire like a bird's feather; and its tube should be half a palm long, and should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of urination is that you take a double thread and tie it to the top of a piece of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread into the syringe; then trim the excess wool and push it all the way up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and henbane juice, and have the patient sit on a chair, and massage the bladder and penis with moistened olive oil and cold water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and when the patient feels that it has reached an empty spot, this is not done according to this order unless for where it guides it wrongly; then stretch out the thread little by little along the wool, and the urine will follow the wool, then pull it out slowly, and let the urine flow; and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient feels relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When pus or blood comes to the bladder, and foul matter accumulates there, and you wish to introduce liquids and medications, use all the instruments which are called "clepsydre," and this is their form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has III holes: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the place where the medicine comes out should be such that it stops up well the tube without addition, so that no moisture can leak, and you can pour in when necessary; and when you wish to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and use the drawer which is inside; thus you will draw the moisture into the catheter, and then push firmly the drawer back in; thus the moisture will enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient can feel it; and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and behind the breast where the ligament falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the liquid you wish to use for enema, then tie between the two breasts firmly with a good double thread, and heat the pot containing this liquid over the fire; then place the tip of the syringe into the rectum, then press your hand on the bladder gradually until the patient feels that all the liquid has come out into the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and cut it roundly around; then put in a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle as one would assemble a sieve, and place inside what you wish of oil and water and liquid, and tie to the instrument; and proceed as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand gradually until all the liquid comes out into the rectum.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the methods of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and I have stated the difference between a stone formed in the kidneys, and all the signs, and when one should operate on stones; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine leaps from the bladder similar to acute urine in its subtlety; and there is hairiness, and the patient's penis itches, and he frequently desires to urinate, and then restrains himself; and many times this jumping of the urine indicates the foundation; and the healing of children until they are four years old is much easier, and becomes very difficult in the elderly, and for young adults it is moderate, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes obstructs the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and lift him up and move him back, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes from a high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be behind his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downward; then search for it and feel inside; if you sense the stone in the area, now quickly cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall when touched all over, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult man; and insert it into his anus, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it towards the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and bring it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand above the groin, and with his left hand remove the skin that is underneath the groin in the area where the incision will be made; then insert the scalpel cutting, which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the groin and the anus, not in the middle but towards the left side of the navel; it should be straight over the stone, and both ends should be close to the anus, with a width sufficient across, and inside narrow according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure will cause what is in the anus to come out without effort; and know that there are some stones which have angles and margins: these are difficult to remove; and there are others which are below, like a thorn, round, from which extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For such cases where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not suffice, then you must clamp with forceps that are like a file at the top to move the stone so that it does not escape; or insert under the instrument a curved one at the tip; and if you cannot manage it thus, widen the opening; and if the blood vessels are injured, clamp them with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first expel the larger one to the neck of the bladder, then work above, and pull out forceful, and the smaller ones afterward.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then you must observe it and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or the urine comes quickly where the flesh cannot heal; but still strive to extract it, using forceps as necessary, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, placing a moist cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lift the patient onto their neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, wash the area very well with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if boils and corrosions come to the wound, and coagulated blood in the bladder, which causes retention of urine, which is known to be passed with the urine: then apply your hand to the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder; then clean the wound with water and asepsis and salt, and help him in all ways you know until he is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you tie his two thighs together, and apply medicines to the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra channel, and stuck inside, so that the urine cannot come out; then treat this as I say, that you cut it many times, but avoid cutting unnecessarily for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron fork in the shape described and have three prongs fixed in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take some thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the fork into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and rotate the fork with your hand on the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from another side; urine will soon come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is immediately broken, and force comes with the urine, and the patient recovers; and if you cannot do this for some reason that prevents it, tie one thread below the stone and another above, then cut the shaft straight through the stone between the two threads, then extract the force, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound; and treat until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stone (kidney stone)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone occurs in women, and if it does happen occasionally, the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows enough to expose herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more embedded than the stone of the man, so it requires a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity mounts upon you, then you must take a midwife who knows well, and at any cost find her, and if you do not find one, by all means seek a skilled physician; and present to her a basin wise in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command that she does what you command concerning the examination of the stone; and carefully see if the woman is a virgin: then it must be put her right hand into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her right hand, and instruct her to put her right hand where the patient's pain is, and search and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gently from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the anus where it is located and feel the stone in that part; do not move her leg above or below the stone, and make the incision small initially; then insert the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone enlarge the wound until the stone can come out freely, and know that there are many kinds of stones: small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with spines.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	know the signs to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood flows from there, place powdered vitriol at the site and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have the instruments I told you about for extracting stones from people to assist in your work; and if the blood continues to flow, which is from the artery that has been cut, apply powder of tents and bendelz to the site and do not repeat this process again, leave the stone where it is and do not try to remove it further, as the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, until the stone has been expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous ramus is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white mucus, which comes from the testicles and contains the egg; it is called "mucus," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so one thinks that it might be another egg; and this occurs between the skin of the testicle and the white mucus we have mentioned; and this happens if there is no pain.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this aquous ramus is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from striking the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: where its color declines to yellow, or without redness, or black, or aqueous white, and these things often occur; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is in the whitish matter that we have said, then the abscesses are frequent, I mean long as the figure of an egg, and do not appear to involve the testicles, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper tissue, then the abscesses are frequent with a part of the egg, and for this reason people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the whitish matter, then one can feel it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try throughout the interstitial area, as its form was described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back on something slightly raised, and place many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and instruct your assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs near the groin area; then take a sharp knife, and cut through the skin of the groin straight from top to bottom up to the white fat tissue, making sure the incision is entirely straight so as not to damage the white fat tissue; then pierce the sac filled with fluid in a wide opening, and remove all the fluid, then place your fingers inside; stretch out the sac upwards, but do not touch the testicles, only the sac itself; cut around it carefully piece by piece, making sure if you don't cut properly, the fluid will return; if the skin moves during your work, reposition it when you finish working on the sac; then stitch together both sides of the groin wound in a single seam, and treat it like other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie off the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the escape of blood; then cut away the suspension completely, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the swelling is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut away the other part as you did the first equally, then dry off the blood, and place in the wound wool moistened in rose oil; and put on another layer of wool moistened in wine and oil, and place the two pieces back, and cover with doubled cloths, and tie it all up according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and wrap them with linen rags according to this appearance and sew them together at the neck of the breeches, and one should cover from the fundament up to the back, and the other at the side; and each of the two ends should be placed above the two angles, and let it all be assembled in a tight band around the navel; and sometimes this branch is treated with fire cautery instead of iron cutting, and you take a fine knife-like cautery, cut through the skin of the swelling, and heat it as we have said, so that the white surface containing the fluid is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that surface at intervals, and scorch it with this fine hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all ways that you can until everything is clean; and guard so that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is safer; and move carefully to prevent blood loss, and treat wounds as needed; and if anything goes against you, whether it be an abscess or bleeding or something else, then cure what opposes you according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then proceed with perforation as I tell you, which is that when you are certain by the signs we have said that watery pus is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then puncture the abscess in the part below all the span wide, and place the puncture along the length of the body; and let the openings be large so that all the fluid can flow out freely; then put cotton over the area, and bind it, and leave it for the remaining fluid to drain, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the fluid to come out from the mouth of the wound, you should place a feather or instrument used for treating the water in hydrops, as described above; expand the small hole of the wound, and know that the fluid will return after six months or around thereabouts, and when it is assembled again as before, then the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there are many fearsome conditions, for which it seems best to leave it as is; and I will tell you about the work and similar aspects of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses occur in the body, especially in the testicles; and this happens for various reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say due to sour excess and acute conditions spread in the testicles, or from impact; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the skin; and there is no pain, but it is a serious abscess; and sometimes an abscess can be fearsome and hard, with redness, and occasionally comes from a blockage in an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it should not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	One who is affected by a swelling of the vein is known by its appearance and expression upon touching with the fingers, and one can properly treat this condition as well as others; cut open the groin area, then place the egg upwards, and draw it out from the white substance, and release the suspensory ligament around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hardened with these new tissues attached, then you should draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is adhered to the white substance or within the vessels, then you must release all of that tissue and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the flesh is at the rear, then you must cut it all away, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, cover the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enclosed in a covering similar to leather, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he moves; and the treatment for this disease is as difficult as the one before, yet we will tell you about it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then place the suspensory of the scrotum down to your hands, covering all the vessels which are close to the penis, and hold them firmly, and stretch them thoroughly; then cut with a broad sharp spatula across the vessels until they are exposed, and then skin off from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then put an awl where there is double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein comes out, and tie it again at the other end; then cut them straight down the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with others when bandaging, so that some vessels fall off which nourish one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if all the vessels come to a vein, it is necessary to draw the testicles to all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment through cutting the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the cheekbone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is through the section that comes from the cheekbone, or by extending it over the abdomen in the area where the angles are, causing the intestines to descend from that fracture into one of the groins; and this rupture can be either from the cheekbone itself, or from its extension, and these two manners come from many causes: such as a blow, jumping, lifting heavy objects, and similar things; and the signs when it is an extension of the cheekbone are gradual over time, not happening suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the bottom because the cheekbone presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is from the section of the cheekbone are that at the beginning a sudden pain appears, and the abscesses vary in appearance, close to the skin, because of the exit of the intestines and the body pushing away from the cheekbone.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the bowel, and are retained inside, causing great pain for the patient, especially when they are constricted.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, for which one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of work is that you instruct the patient to push his intestines back into the wound with his hand if it can be reintroduced; then tie a string around his neck between your hands, lift his thighs; then stretch his abdomen above, and cut all the skin from the groin down long; then insert scissors according to what you need to open the wound so that the eggs may come out; then scrape off the tough white fat under the skin of the groin until it is exposed on all sides; then place your index finger in the space behind the testicle, between the tough white fat beneath the skin of the scrotum and the second layer of fat; and move the part that lies behind the testicle between the second layer of fat;
