then move with your right hand inside the abdomen of the scrotum, stretch the tough white fat up to your left hand, lift the testicle towards the waist with all the fat; instruct the assistant to lift the testicle up and untie what is tied behind it; ask them both if there are any intestines wrapped around the tough white fat, and if you find anything, put it under the belly beneath it; then take a needle with I thick thread made of X threads, and place it in the back part of the fat, which is after the skin of the scrotum behind the waist; then cut the parts that appear from the threads until there are IIII threads; then arrange them one over another like a cross, and bind the fat we spoke of under the scrotal skin tightly with two strong ties; then wrap around the threads and tie them firmly on both sides so that none of the vessels nourishing it can enter inside, lest an abscess occur there; then put back the bandage according to the first long bandage II fingers wide, and after these two bandages leave uncovered a large part of one finger width under the scrotal skin; and after all this in accordance with the roundness that the testicle carries; then cut the part beneath the scrotal skin until there is no raw flesh or bowels, as we mentioned before; then apply wet wool soaked in oil to the wounds, and put on the bandage we spoke of.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white vein that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the ligature until it falls off on its own; and if it delays in falling, soak it in warm water, and place what we have said upon it, until it falls off; then treat the wound with another method, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the condition where the intestines are involved, in such a way that you bind the vessels, above the navel lightly on the back; then cut into them and treat the abscess as we have described, until the vessels fall off; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a rupture in the groin area, as we have said, and the location is apparent; and no part of the intestines descends to the genitals, but if they do descend, it is dangerous and requires constant attention; and yet if it remains too long at this point, the wound or hernia grows worse until the intestines descend further. This happens due to the extension of the hernia in the groin area, as we have mentioned, because it extends, then softens, swells, and becomes apparent. The treatment for this is by cautery, as we have previously stated; sometimes it is treated with iron in this way: the patient lies supine on their back between your hands, and you cut around the swollen area according to its size of three fingers width; then remove the hernia that lies under the skin, take out the needle and place it over the visible part of the hernia; press firmly against the abdomen, sew up both sides of the visible hernia on top of the needle, and sew one side and the other; then pull out the head of the needle, and do not cut into the hernia or stretch the skin as I have told you in the treatment of the rupture of the intestines; finally, treat it according to the method for treating wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, wrap and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The tissue is tense, and there is no appearance of tearing, and the cauterizations are soft in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the scrotum is often softened in some men because the tissues inside are softened and appear milky; and when it needs to be treated, make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then stitch together the two edges at one seam; if you wish, sew off the excess soft skin in three or four places firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and leave the stitches.
dou chastrement	of the chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is condemned in our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; yet it is necessary for two reasons: one is knowing how to answer when asked about it and knowing the treatment; the other is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by traction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become softened and hang down; then hold them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: you must first anesthetize the animal, and press the skin around the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut each testicle in one stroke after thoroughly scraping them; and leave some of the fatty tissue and the fine fat on top of the vessels; this method of castration is gentler than that done by attraction, because with attraction there may remain some part of the testicles accidentally, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	On hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways among men: one is that between the two testicles it has the form of a woman's genitalia as nature intended for women, and sometimes it also has pubic hair, and at other times it urinates there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and place upon the wrist as with a rod and two eggs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut away the adjacent tissues, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the scrotum, there is no specific treatment.
de la tentigene	of tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a tissue attached to the genital area, so that it appears too large and unsightly; some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the condition.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should stain the excess of the tentigene with your hand or fingernails and cut it lightly; do not go too deep so that no blood flows, then treat it further until it is healed; and for another part that appears at the entrance of the vagina, remove it, and sometimes it may bleed, and resembles a hernia, and because of this they called it by the ancients "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you treat it as we have said regarding tenacity, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of the woman's body is not perceived, or when the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has come upon her; or it is caused by adhering flesh, or thick mucus, and forms perfectly in the womb, or in the ribs, or elsewhere; and it prevents conception and childbirth, and possibly menstruation; and knowledge of this is gained through examination.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstruction is apparent and close, then treat it with your fingers or with something straight.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle syfac (a type of swelling or sore), and it is near the two books (likely referring to anatomical locations), then hurry and do as follows: place your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch out the two books firmly, until the subtle syfac is laid bare, and be over the swelling; then take linen, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the area, and let the woman rest for a man each day, so that she cannot stand up.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syfac is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a scalpel similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh growth, suspend it by a hook and cut it; and have medicines that stop bleeding, such as hellebore, dragon's blood, incense, along with plenty of egg whites; then bandage the wound with a strip of cloth wide enough so that the wound cannot close; and in this way treat it for a long time, and cover the area with a dry linen dressing; and continue treating it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh becomes infected in a wound, it must be cut according to this method, except for deeply seated abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the deep-seated abscess that is in the wound, one must not attempt to cut it.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are protrusions of veins that usually occur without cause, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn hard; and we have already mentioned in the section their appearances, and the signs, and I will say here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when hemorrhoids and hard lumps are thoroughly in the wound and do not respond to sensation, they cannot be cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have the mouth of the boil, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by lancing.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the altar with tongs, and cut it at its roots; then apply powder of medicines that constrict blood, such as hawthorn berries and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, seat her in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and grease, and make a plaster for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping to the back and breasts without injuring them; then take flax, and soak it in juice of plantain or agrimony with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, treat the area with ointment until it is well; and what is called "albathir" is red, similar to a pustule, so it must be lanced as I said about the thulul; then treat it until it is well.
des apostemes de la marris	for abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as ulcers and stony abscesses and herpes and carbuncles and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes in the thigh, which is not of those abscesses that are collected by bowe; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die down until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have two small chairs where he can lean, and support his back and bring together his feet towards the side of the thigh; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then give him some medicine towards his right side, and administer the instrument used for working on the mouth of the thigh, the form of which follows afterward; and it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument, you insert the tip first to know the depth of the thigh, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go too deep and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the thigh with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause it pain; and it is necessary for him to place the horn part of the instrument above, and to hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is cut with a hand tool gently, then you should cut off the top, at the spatumile line; and when the pus is emptied out, you must place in the wound moistened cloths in rose oil or in green oil; and put the cloth towards the edge of the wound and on the inside wool clean wetted with water or mallows cooked; then cure after two days of ointment application, as needed until it heals; and sometimes lift up the wound and the pus by enema of water and honey, and then of water where long roots of lily and aristolochia are boiled; then return to applying ointments.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in the flesh, then you must avoid treating it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing downward, and desiring to smell the air: then you know that the child hastens to come forth; at that time you know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and the exit is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends with its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the woman is purified of her superfluities by good purification; and he who comes forth in another manner does not come forth naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes up onto its feet, and comes forth with the buttocks, or the hands, or it comes out over its belly, or in a sitting position, and is turned around by chance on its neck, and by other evil figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head naturally, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and if her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle-like seat which women use; and prepare an ointment of oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place in her mouth the small spoon from which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the membrane, and apply it to her fingernail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and press the woman's abdomen so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to administer an enema of fenugreek musilage with sesame oil; then make her sneeze from condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: the child will now emerge.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands exit forcefully, then you must reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then lift the chair onto the ground, and support the woman so she does not fall when standing up; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, cut off the hands with the knife that is placed here beforehand, extract the child, and reset them evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of delivering the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it is necessary to push it upwards; then turn it bit by bit until it is straight; then take one of its feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps to the thighs, then command it to be seized, and make it sneeze with condii; if it jumps further away, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go back as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come back as we have said, take muscillage of aloes, and oil of sesamum, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; then place the woman's nature within and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to below her ribs; when she is moistened below, apply the colic of myrrh and put it underneath, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her abdomen, for now the child will jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place its hands little by little on its knees; then lift it up onto its neck, and let the feet hang down, and lay it flat on the bed; then bend its hands little by little, and then take its hands onto its belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until she is prepared to go downward; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them around, then move the belly upwards, then place your hands there; and bring out the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold on as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child that comes with one hand hanging out
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the midwife to return the hand: if she cannot return it, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lie her on the bed, and raise her legs fully; then administer the massage that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and according to the natural figure of the child, make her sneeze, and command her to grip so that the child may come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the exit of the child onto its neck, and have her spread her hands, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the midwife to hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and do so gently; and when it is even, place on it the natural massage of salt and oil as we have said, then command her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to applying force in this manner throughout the entire second stage, cut the membrane at your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the fetus can move on its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not obstructed and allow the fetus to move; then insert the child gently until you have placed it as necessary, and instruct the woman to hold herself in some way: then extract it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	on the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins often come into the world, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, though it does occasionally happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if one can call them that; I know them to be multiplied, and are separated by the surface which divides them, which is attached to the bud; and sometimes they issue as naturally as one tooth beneath another, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue severely, treat them as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and do quickly and gently what it does; and do so as it moves toward health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or sometimes up to XV, and are completely formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and it is necessary that the bandage be careful with them, because similar things may happen; do accordingly as is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child in her womb, as I said in the division, and nothing comes out, and you are forced to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman has healthy strength, and has not had an accident where she fears death; it is necessary that the woman lie on her back, and have her legs inclined downward, and her feet raised; and the assistant holds two towels, or one is tied to the bed so that it does not obstruct the descent of the child; then rub the mouth with marri mixed with moist oil made from hellebore and fenugreek seeds, and oil of flaxseed; then apply these oils and mixtures to her hands; then gently press into the marri; then find a suitable place where she can grip the hooks that are comfortable for her; check if the child is prepared to come down headfirst; then insert the hook in her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or behind the chin, or at the jawbone or near the sides; and if the descent is feet-first, fix it in the thighs and middle ribs; she should hold the hook with her right hand, place the handle between both fingers of her left hand, gently press with her whole hand, insert the hook into one of these places we mentioned until something gives way; this is how to use the hook.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then spread them evenly by moving from one side to the other, to facilitate their exit, and let the hooks be toothed to hold onto the flesh, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, smear one of its sides with some oil, and push it into that part, and pull the other part; and if anything remains, place this hook a bit higher up, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and it cannot be brought back for grasping, you must wrap around the finger until it fully emerges; then cut at the joint or at the side, and similarly you must do this with the other hand, and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow at the exit, or there is a fever assembled in the head, then you must insert the spatumile spine between your two fingers, and cut open the head and remove the fluid; or you can shave it with the instrument called "almidach", of which the form comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and thus also do if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pincers, and if the head jumps out and is stuck to the forcele, cut it so that the moisture inside the narrow exit flows out; and if it cannot flow out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the socket is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is tight in the belly or the thigh, you must stretch him with the finger wrapped around the hand; and cut into the belly or thigh until the moisture inside flows out; and if another limb is removed and the head remains, then he should place his thumb firmly against the socket, and pull it up to the mouth of the socket; then put in a hook or two, and force them forward; and if the mouth of the socket is narrow due to a hot abscess that has come upon it, you must not work on it but rather administer moist and fatty things; and use poultices, and apply solutions that soften and moisten.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it level, then treat as we have said for the living child; and if one has no power, cut it up in pieces, and leave nothing of the placenta.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat as we have said for large abscesses that come with fever; and if there is excessive bleeding, put it on water compresses, and treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had been dead, then another was conceived upon that one, and the other was also stillborn.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, abscesses came in her mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began to discharge heavily.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied an ointment of strong attraction, and out came a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for there are no bones in the abdomen.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I treated the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was in a much better condition; and I kept the woman under treatment for a long time, and she continued to discharge pus from the site; and I recall this chapter only because when masters encounter an unusual thing, they should seek help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the binder, which the books have; and for two turns to the two shoulders of the two arms.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the handles should be more delicate than the binder, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the rod should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the wood one finger thick; and its length a palm and a half; and between the two arms there should be two joints of the same rod, which are firmly fixed in each, about half a palm long or slightly more; and these two joints are placed at the mouth of the joint to open when turning the two handles.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony wood or boxwood, resembling pincers; and let it have two heads with attachments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vagina with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and her legs spread apart, then insert the two attachments together into the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument as you did with the pincers equally, according to the amount by which you wish to open the mouth of the vagina, until it gives way as much as she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all adorned at the top, and their appearances are varied; and when physicians have them prepared, they become more eager to perform their work, and they appear greater to people according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze by tickling her; and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, so much the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in its cover, then place herbs that can open the mouth of the patient inside it, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cascara sagrada, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled or cooked in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the pot hole, and the other end into the patient's mouth, and hold it so that the steam enters the patient; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second joint jumps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not move, as commanded to the patient that she moisten her left hand in linseed oil or mallow juice, and then place it on the affected area, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straightly so that the tissue does not tear during extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and to the left, and then drawn out; it will come forth and dislodge.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the tissue is tight, we have described the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not move from any of what we have said, be careful that you do not pull too hard; but it must be that which is at the opening of the tissue, tie it to the woman's thigh, then give her a clyster of tetrafarmacos ointment; this will relieve and reset it, and it will move; however, when she passes it, if there comes an unpleasant odor in the stomach and head, and it disfigures the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be given to them: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for the retention of menstruation and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass, resembling a tube, with the tip finely placed in the body, and the ends wide over the fire; and let the fumigation be above the coals, and continue until the smoke is exhausted, then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but instead it is sealed with a small syphilis-like condition: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that seal properly, and not with an overly sharp instrument, and be careful not to injure them; then place wet wool in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that he will not stay in bed, place a chain through the bedpost, and leave it there for his hands to ensure he remains until he wishes to go to chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from the sudden closure of a wound or abscess; it is necessary to cut that closure: treat it as we have said about the chain for keeping someone in bed.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from inside the anus are nodations, and those that come near or between the two parts may have one fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it works, and often moisture turns white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating; they are known by what comes out in defecation or flatulence when the patient expels waste, and perhaps worms come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they reach to the knee joint, and to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula penetrates to the anus or not: and it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a fine needle of linen or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, insert a fine thread of flax or horsehair until you feel the thread with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no passage to excretion or wind or anything else appears, as we have said: then you know that it does not penetrate; hurry to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, then he urinates through it, and cannot be cured by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it reaches to the joint of the thigh, then the swelling comes up to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the pain is around it, then it will quickly become a bow (ankylosis), and medicine or treatment by ointment is useless; and in these fistulas reaching such points, there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not perforated and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back; and raise his legs up to his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then insert a probe of linen, or lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the probe goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should place your index finger there; if you sense that the skin has been pierced; and where you feel between your finger and the flesh is exposed, you know it is perforated; do not treat it further as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says that it can be well healed in some cases, but this happens rarely; and the aid one does for it is to heat the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and insert it entirely hot into the fistula until it reaches near the fundament; and do this twice or three times, until you know that the unhealthy tissue has been burned, which appears like a feather; and then dress it with moistened cloths in butter until the flesh grows back, and afterwards treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth and unites.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he cannot be healthy otherwise; and if the fistula enters, but does not penetrate to the root which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or fatty tissue between your thumb and the fistula, and you see the fistula under that which covers the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward until you reach the base of the fistula, and apply the cautery afterward, until it reaches the head of the fistula; and the fistula will be freed and fall out; then clean those damaged tissues that look like a feather quill, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood fails you, and it cuts between you and the task, then cauterize with fire or with astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery combines two good things: it burns away excess flesh and stops blood and dries moisture; then treat with wet cloths dipped in butter or crushed herbs until the wound bleeds, and thus the burned flesh is removed from the wound; then treat the wound with ointments made of hard substances that stick to the flesh, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up from deep in the anus and is distant from the body, place your finger inside the anus and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between two layers of tissue or flesh where it is close to piercing, there must be no doubt but rather faith and hope through one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, cut it to its base, or if you can place tents and treat it as described first; do not go too deep so that you do not cut into the tissue holding the anus, and let defecation occur naturally; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove the covering and cleanse it after cutting near the anus, whether by tent or other appropriate instrument; then clean the infected flesh in the wound as much as possible; then work to restore the wound and divert the fistula to a part outside the anus: this is easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it reaches to the bottom near the skin above, take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you wind the thread around point II, and insert the probe along the entire thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated in the margin of the base inwardly, then withdraw the thread from that hole, so you press your finger against the base; and pull out the tip of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and hold them to each other, and leave it for one or two days; and rewrap the thread occasionally, until the thread passes through the tissues between them and they adhere; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to treat deep incisions by cutting them open and then curing them as we have said, until they are healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous process where one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other, because one should not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those inside the anus, like grains of resin, which can be small or large, and contain blood. There may be one or several, some near the anus and others at its head; but those further away have less moisture, sometimes containing a little yellow liquid or a little blood, with the color of flesh. The treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit down in chambers until they are expelled, and then gently grasp them with your fingernail, holding them firmly, then cut them off at their roots; if the fingernail cannot hold due to moisture, use a probe or cotton, or a piece of linen, to extract them by hand, then cut them and apply warm powder cautery as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization. Cauterize them as described there, and treat further until they are healed; if the anus cannot expel them, administer an enema with a harsh and bitter solution to clean what is inside the anus so it can be expelled easily; when this happens, if the filaments are out of the anus, treatment is easier. Grasp them with your fingernail or forceps, cut them off, then treat as we have said until they are healed, and beware of cutting with an iron instrument.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you manage the suturing in this manner: take twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread from above and make the needle pierce from another side, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; then firmly tie the thread, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one to drain excess blood; then place a moistened piece of cloth in rose oil or cerate on the foundation, and place over the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave them until they defecate, and when they have passed, treat them with ointment and other care, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the anus or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of feces in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should incise with the point of a scalpel or your nail on the surface above it, without letting it dry; then treat it until it is healed as necessary; and if it cannot heal, then shave more vigorously than before, until it bleeds much and becomes scraped; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small rash that appears on the body and spreads very quickly; and sometimes it is caused by cold, and one feels it like death from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place the quill over the swelling, so that the circles completely encircle the swelling; then turn your hand around the whole quill until you cut all around the swelling, and embed it perfectly, and strip the swelling of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a thread of linen or iron according to this form, and let it be fine underneath and drawn over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the threads in place and press them together. And if you wish, cauterize the swelling as described earlier in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a enema is made of silver or endive, or of melted silk or barley; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to the needs of those who receive them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who treat children and those who are weak and in pain use small ones.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is as follows, and the abdomen is bandaged in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be spacing where the abdomen is bandaged as you see, and the head should be pierced from inside; and have two holes on one side and one on the other; and let the abdomen where the medicine is placed be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and pierce it all around with small holes, and there should be a finger's width between each hole, then insert a strong cord through these holes ten times or more around, and secure the abdomen like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then administer the enema; this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a gentle enema of oil or honeyed egg yolk, or something similar, then pour it in gently; then massage the patient with both hands evenly, until he is thoroughly treated, then remove the enema, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, there will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema in a case of diarrhea where the medicine wants to come out quickly, repeat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or an abscess, then the enema should be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema wherein the skin should be stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the section the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you about the treatments by hand and with medication, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds vary according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are due to the falling of stones, and the cutting of swords and knives, or lances or staffs or arrows, or similar things; where they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls upon the neck, or upon the head, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and other members; and I shall tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from falling of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound large, and you fear the formation of a hot abscess: then I treat it immediately with a cephalic dressing if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the dressing be opposite to the injured part; and avoid letting the patient have an excess of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be bled, then let his food be light, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses are coming, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the fresh wound that has not been exposed to air, powder which I will mention shortly; and if it has become inflamed due to exposure, then apply some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then sew them together as I will say about belly wounds, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone and barely hangs on by a little piece, cut it off; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as brains and cooked wheat, like porridge, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrid flesh in the skin that is not adhering to the bone, cut away all the rotten parts and wash it clean, then cure it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched with medicines, tie off the vessel, and if you find it dislocated, ligate it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy: it is that you put in this powder which seals as though the flesh has grown back.
