Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely grind the powder, apply it to the wound, and press firmly until it sticks well and adheres to all its blood; then bind it tightly, and do not loosen it if it does not swell; for you should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses only charcoal when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the wound should heal as though it has grown back.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in summer, do not apply this powder; but put on some digested ointments, or porridge made of barley flour with water and honey, until it runs fluid; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there should be no other treatment than to leave it alone and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; nor should any cold substance be applied to the wound, as the nature of the nerve is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with sweet water, and rose oil, and cucumber washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, then pierce them at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then open it, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine in the throat or the windpipe is cut, where the passage of air lies, sew the throat over the windpipe, but do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural form; and then bind it carefully, and leave it for several days, then treat with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has caused an impression in the bone, then cure it; and if there are pieces of bone, take them out as far as you can, and those that you cannot remove, let them be until the wound suppurates, and let it be released and its exit cleared; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle with the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then check if the wound causes swelling as the patient moves: you will then know that the wound is fatal; but if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first hour, nor bind it for the blood that does not flow deeply, or it may go to the heart and kill the patient; instead, apply an attracting ointment, and bandage it twice a day. If you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient rest on the wound for three days, four, or more; there will be no spasm, nor trembling from heart trouble or strangeness of breathing; and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments until he is healed; and if she cannot heal him, and you work, then you know there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it as such; if it is large, stitch it; if it is small, powder it; and if it is pressed against the bone, even if pieces have been severed, seek to heal the wound, and treat exposed tendons if they are separated; and if they are not separated, leave the wound to run freely, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is large and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, causing an infection; and the suturing is more difficult, and at times a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because if one does not immediately replace the intestines, they will retract further due to swelling upon feeling cold; thus a smaller rupture can be more troublesome. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four manners: two common sutures happen with abdominal surgery, and the other wounds of the body share similar suturing techniques, yet these are specifically adapted for abdominal repairs; and I will explain each one separately and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, it is difficult to replace, which can be done in one of two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or piece of cloth in hot water only, which you boil with vinegar and cedar and spice, and rinse the intestines until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use wine that constricts to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water in which hellebore and mallows have been boiled, for this gradually opens the entrance; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment should be cautious, as one should not cut without great necessity; and here is the instrument for making the incision: cut inwardly along the curvature and do not go outward, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, put them back in their natural form in their proper place if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the abdomen, you must have the patient lie on his back with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the front part of the abdomen, place the head and feet higher than the affected parts; and similarly, if there is a rupture in one of the two parts, raise the injured part higher than the other; and thus you must treat what I say regarding large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds apply what is suitable, then hold in your hand a minister who can cover the entire wound with their hand and bring together the edges; this is the common method of suturing. Take one needle or more according to the width of the wound, leaving an inch from the edge of the wound, and place a strong thread on the needle; pierce both sides of the skin with the two layers inside the skin until you have pierced it thoroughly, and bring together the four corners; then double the thread around the needle in two places, and bring together the two edges of the wound, leaving another inch, and insert another needle; tie the knot as you did for the first needle, and continue this method according to your need for needles until the entire wound is closed. The needles should be medium-sized, between fine and thick, because thin needles cut through all flesh, while overly thick ones cannot enter properly: therefore, they should be medium. Do not insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, as they might damage the wound before it heals; then trim the ends of the needles so they do not injure the patient when sleeping, and place cotton or fabric on the needle tips to keep them in place until the wound has healed. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds. A second common method is to bring together both sides of the skin and inner layers with one strong thread; once you have pierced all four corners thoroughly, wind the needle back at the point where you started, as when sewing cloth; leave an inch between each suture. This suturing technique can be performed by anyone. I myself sutured a wound in someone's abdomen caused by a knife, which was about one hand-width wide and from which intestines protruded for two hand-widths, situated right in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until the fifteenth day, and I treated him, and he became well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honeyed water until he became well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the flesh straight through, attach the thread where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inner part outward again; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as tailors do with skins, leaving one side of the thread on one side and taking it up on the other until the entire seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: one brings together the two parts naturally and applies one end of the suture to the other end in such a manner: insert a needle at the nearest peak of the wound, piercing only that spot, leaving the two ends of the skin; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner part through both sides of the skin; then pierce each one from the outer part to the inner part through two other peaks on the opposite side; this is the most common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this and some people attest to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having its own thread; and you must insert one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and note that when the rupture is inside the abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than for ruptures in other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as though the surgeon had moved it, reset the intestines, and sewn; then put on healing powder, and if the surgeon has moved it, apply any ointment available until the wound drinks [absorbs]; and stitch the wound, and let the sifac [wound surface] and the mirach [wound margins] be sealed; then treat the wound as other wounds are treated until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, apply old cotton immediately when it begins to drink pus, twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many conditions where the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound will affect the principal members, it is necessary to moisten light wool in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles [corners], and below the flanks; and if pain or putrefaction occurs in the bowels, which often happens, then administer an enema of boiled black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inwardly, and note that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back as you would with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or green, then you must tie off the area that is black so that no more blood comes out, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ligament, and make the two ends hang from below the wound up to where they fall when the spleen drops, so that the extraction is easier when it falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I saw a man pierced in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became infected and turned into a fistula, from which his excretions and wind escaped; I treated it according to what I could, and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the tissue closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it close, I feared the patient would have pain in his abdomen; but he had none, and remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated as follows: take thread with large needles, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the needle has opened its way through, place it between the two edges so that they press against each other; then cut off the head of the needle, which remains securely fastened, and put another needle in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is sewn up; and suture the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head of the intestine becomes inflamed and does no harm to the patient, one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the tip of this intestinal thread so it is very clean, then twist a thin linen thread around the tip, put the thread on a needle, and sew the intestine closed, and tie it securely at the wound; and this method of stitching wounds is not far from the way of trust and hope; if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no remedy or healing, unless it is done with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess when it suppurates is generally called a "fistula", and especially when it is hollowed out and penetrates the bone.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth an improper knot hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it is also hollow like the quill of a bird; and sometimes it pierces clear bone, and other times thickly; sometimes it is small, and other times quite large; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound which does not heal and has no flesh growing back must be due to one of the IX causes: namely, by the thinness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard tissue inside, on the edges, preventing new flesh from growing; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter has poor quality; or the medicine in treatment is not good; or due to corruption being like a plague; or due to the property of the region being slow digestion, delayed health, swollen by nature; or it contains veins or bone: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and medicinal cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is now necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and some affect the main property of a limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to cure, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I mentioned, and you have confidence in its treatment, and want to know it, take a probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, then insert it; and if the fistula is tortuous, search it with a fine probe made of lead, because lead can bend around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has several openings and you cannot properly examine it with probes, irrigate through one of the openings, as moisture passes from one opening to another, and clean it; then carefully press with your hand until you know if there is bone or nerve in its path, and ask well of the patient about the pain they feel when you press, and where they feel it; and once you truly know where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the places I told you, then cut it according to what I said, and remove all rotten flesh inside; then cure it until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply straight, you must cut deep as possible, then place moistened probes in medicine to dissolve the excess material at the bottom; and then apply ointments that heal flesh until it is healed; and if it does not heal with this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not cause you trouble in the principal members as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all corruption is gone, then treat with healing substances until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns to its previous state, know that you have not reached the depth: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the site; and if it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can pull with forceps, extract it with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, remove them all without leaving any; and if the moisture resists you, and there is no error or fear, cut through both flesh and moisture, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, place on the wound something that raises putrefaction, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until the blackness is all taken away, then restore the wound; and if there is much part of the corrupted tissue reaching to the bone substance, you must scrape and cut it out entirely up to the corruption, then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened in a man's leg so that you take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came inside the body, such that the substances reached his leg and it swelled with a large abscess. There was no cause to let out fluid by opening it; but the doctors, in their folly, operated on it until they opened the abscesses, removing much matter, and it became a fistula, with many holes through which all the body's fluids and moisture leaked. Many doctors treated him for about two years without any skilled hand in the art, until I was called to see his leg and the medicines used to treat him; what came out of the holes was large and his flesh turned red, and he had a yellow complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and perforated, with the corruption reaching deep into the bone; I removed what appeared to be the corrupted bone, thinking there would be no further corruption beyond what I took away; and began to treat the wound with internal medicines for a long time, but it could not heal; then I started again, cutting into the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, so I removed it, and tried to close the site; however, I could only cut around one palm's width of the bone, and then treated it with medicines until it healed rapidly, but further work was unnecessary except for the patient’s weakness which could not endure, and my fear of death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there was an evacuation of blood, but he remained completely healthy, and in the place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he had good health with no harm or contrary effect whether going or coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows: take a piece of linen, and tie it to the end of the visible bone, and instruct someone to stretch it upwards; and place another thicker piece of woolen cloth over the skin covering the bone, and extend the upper part so that you pull the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the skin where you wish to treat, so that the poultice does not irritate the skin; and place a cautery or a board under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh; and continue treating until the corruption can be seen and felt no more, and repeat treatment as necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear clearly, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place a hot coal underneath, and then lay thread from one side to the other across the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint and sew the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy than cutting; and if the corruption is at the finger joint of the hand or foot, it is very strong that thing, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you; and purify it in all manners as you can, but let not the vein or nerve oppose you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to provide each kind of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the ways of diseases; thus consider the instrument of which you have need according to what it suits.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot from within or due to external causes; and when you have treated that corrosion with medicine but it does not help, then it is necessary to amputate the limb up to where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this means of death, or by the greater evil of losing the limb; and the signs are that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and rots afterwards, for the corruption spreads from limb to limb, and takes over throughout the body; therefore hasten to amputate, and if it is due to the bite of venomous beasts such as sea scorpion or wyrm and similar, and the corrosion is at the head of the hand, then cut it off, and do not give any space for it to come up to the arm.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, death is certain, and no remedy will suffice except for the amount of its virtue; and do the same when the corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cover at the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cover the entire foot; and if it climbs up the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or covering the limb is that you bind both above and below, and extend one minister with a ligature downward, and another minister upward, and cut through the flesh between the two ligatures at one span wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cover it, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the dressing does not touch healthy skin, and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the area quickly or apply some powder to constrict it; then return to your medicine until it is complete, and bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in this matter: there came upon him a blackness which seemed like a burn from fire, and that corrosion began first on his big toe, spreading over the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to amputate the foot, and was healed; and after much time it returned to his thumb of the hand, and he came to me, and I applied things that would repel it after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corrosion; and he vowed that I should cut off his hand, but I did not wish to do so, hoping instead to repel the material; and also feared that if I were to amputate his hand, he might die, as his constitution was weak; and in despair he returned home and hurriedly amputated his hand himself, and was healed; and I have only told this story for those who would act differently, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and persists for so long that it accumulates a large amount of pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving behind a cavity like a vessel; and the skin above is as delicate as fine linen, not reaching to the bone or nerve, and such diseases are called "sinus", and are not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, it is called "fistula"; and when you cut this skin all around, especially when it is delicate like fine linen; and it does not heal despite its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you trust that the skin will heal and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema as follows: check if the breast is swollen, and the pus coming from it has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take equal parts of wax, oil, and litharge, put them in a vessel over fire until the mixture turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take this according to your need, dilute it with water and honey, and administer it as an enema while pinching the anus closed; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then expel it gently squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed of its foulness; if the patient cannot tolerate this or the Egyptian medicine, use an enema made from ash water: take vine wood ashes and pour water over them, strain it, and administer as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleansed; if neither works for the patient, give an enema of water and honey with a little litharge powder mixed in or honey and wine mixed together, where the honey has the property to cleanse and wash, while the wine promotes healing; once this is done and you trust that the breast is thoroughly cleansed, administer an enema made from medicine that stimulates tissue growth such as diaphoretic plaster mixed with rose oil and red wine, or use other medicines and ointments whose properties I have mentioned in the section on ointments; if the opening of the breast is small and the catheter cannot enter, widen it slightly with a probe and place an Egyptian ointment cloth or basilicon over it until it fits; if the wound is too large, stitch it up leaving only one area where the enema can be administered, and if the pus issuing from the opening is above, cut lower down to allow proper administration.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the boil is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate; and if you cannot cut below the breast as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the boil runs downward to the lowest place where it is; for when the boil is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate; and if you cannot cut below the breast as you wish, prepare it in this manner: so that the boil runs slightly down, and leave nothing of the boil behind; then apply medicines that consolidate the healthy tissue and spread a linen cloth covering all the healthy part; then cut at the force points the opening of the chest somewhat larger than the first one, and place another ointment according to the size of the opening on the wound to alleviate the boil, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days once; and that which is over the opening of the chest, remove often to remove the boil, and examine what flows from the boil whether it is venom or little or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; and be wary if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see that nature jumps over the opening of the wound, know that the healing process begins and health approaches; then release the dressing in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom strikes after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people for whom meat delayed in their wounds is harmful, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes up from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if the digestion is slow and prolonged, add drying medicines in substance but dry in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, because it contains much vitriol, which is one of the final remedies; prepare a diaphoretic ointment made with rose oil, mixed evenly in substance with old wine; then thicken and use it. The same can be better prepared if enriched by cooking when no diaphoretic ointment is available: take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them together, powder them over honey while it is on the fire; then glue a cloth to it, spread it on the stomach, sometimes administering aristology, long roots of celestial lilies, which are like fine flour of vervain and centaury; use these simple or compound remedies: crush them into powder and mix with the honey as mentioned above, and use it. If the condition persists without improvement after such treatment, then understand that the corruption is deep-seated and has made an impression in the bone, or on hard parts, or ligaments; treat it as a fistula cure, as we have said previously.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises from underneath the nail of the hand or foot, or sometimes it may occur in other toes; and when it ages and goes untreated, a foul abscess comes, running and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and at times it may spread entirely; and corrosion reaches to the bone, causing a putrid pain, and the head of the toe becomes swollen, and its color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment is of no use, then you must cut away all the excess that remains around the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses against the flesh, and it begins to hurt, and bleeds, then you must place the cautery under the nail that is hurting the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away the affected flesh gently and lightly, and apply medicines that are burning and corrosive to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and pull it out, for as long as the bone remains corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see that part of it is rotten, then cut off from there as was mentioned earlier, then treat until it heals; and if it is pierced and infected, and feels great pain, then you must first cleanse it; then carefully cut the nail diagonally in such a way that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the stiffness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joint that is born in the hands of some men is entirely flesh, and sometimes it has bones, and occasionally there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, where the origin is in some ways different from the others.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with a nodule on the joint do not move, and those who are born at the finger joint sometimes do move; the size of the one that is flesh is very small, in this manner: measure it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be careful with cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the back side, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone in one stroke appropriate for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by inflammation of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut that swelling so that the parts repair according to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or moistened cloths in rose oil, so they do not swell again; or put between two pieces of fine wool, until the area is healed as needed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of the two with the palm, cut that swelling as needed.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick and covered, full of melancholic excesses, which occur in many parts of the body; and they happen more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer enemas to them at times, and then treat them with basilik.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The treatment by phlebotomy is according to this method: first apply a hot water bath very strongly to the leg until thick blood becomes thin, then lift the patient's leg from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut into one vein or two or three places in one large incision, then raise and draw out black blood with your hand from one side to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can endure; and then bind it up, and instruct him to take food that promotes black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the vein is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by fire, then cut straight into the vein from the ankle to the top of the knee, or in the part below the calf; then work on the skin with an incision knife, and strip the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; then lift up the underside of the vein as much as it is raised from the skin, and then gently scrape it with another lancet as you did before; then cut another length, or several if needed, then raise it, and cut to the toe joint, then pull and raise until the second length; then strip it from length to length until it comes out entirely, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle through the entire double thread, tie and pull it, and insert another pin underneath, and turn your hand back and forth, until it is out; and beware that it does not break, for if it breaks, one cannot pull or raise it, causing harm to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, place on the wound site wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not sever it; and pull it out as we have stated before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved and does not cut, so as not to sever the vein; it is thickly curved, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein originates in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil where there is little moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as it occurs within the body like serpents and worms, arising between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then it changes its place, and the vein begins to come out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap it around a piece of linen from one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it up, and leave the bandage hanging down the leg; every time it comes loose, rewrap it around the bandage and tie it again. If it is too long, cut off part of it but do not cut it at its root until it has completely come out, for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh causing an abscess and putrefaction in that place, leading to a bad illness; this must be treated little by little until there is nothing left in the body. Sometimes this vein can be five hand breadths long when treated or ten, and once I had a case where it came out ten hand breadths long, and when you cut it, one rib or hole will burst open, so pierce it all the way through to let everything come out; empty the matter inside, then apply medicines that clear putrefaction for some days, and treat it as you would abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is smaller, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there comes much difficulty, and from which it often bleeds; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of ox", because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body ascending and descending, and one can feel it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and causes pain; and it arises from putridity of some humors, just as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids come from the intestines; and there is fear of its malice, because when it travels throughout the body, if it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance it can enter, and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it needs to be incised and drained, one cannot forcefully do so: therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut over it and drain it out; if the vein is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it stops bleeding; the greatest harm it causes is that it may affect the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye on the head, firmly hold below the eyebrow, then cut over it and drain it out; and the patient must use cleansing of the body with medicines dissolving bad humors and refrain from food causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and then can move from one limb to another; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it move up to the shoulder as quickly as a worm does, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it kept circling around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
