Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had heard of many who had seen pain move from one place to another, but I had never witnessed it myself as I did in the woman; and I thought that this was because women have dry bodies, and veins exposed, and for this reason such windiness appears constrained; and it does not appear according to this reasoning in those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to treat this disease and the patient feels that pain, if it shows itself as we have said, lift it up and down quickly, and then cut into the place where that constrained windiness is; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, treat it as one would for dispelling winds, such as with fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large points, small points, barbed points, and fixed points; and those with two angles, and some with tongues, and others with pieces; and when an arrow strikes any limb, it does so in two ways: either it strikes a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes any part of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you next, become apparent: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death often follows in such cases; and when these ominous signs do not appear and the arrow is not deeply seated, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and strikes the dura mater which is over the brain, are scotoma and blindness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes bloodless fluid issues from the nostrils or ears; and by chance speech and voice may be lost; and from the wound flows white moisture like pus, and also as if it were a bruise on flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then hold yourself ready for the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left mammary region, and feels as if it were embedded in a hard object, not empty; and sometimes the arrow moves like pus, and forms black blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope: then you know without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that strikes the abdomen is that foamless saliva spits from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the back of the thigh, it is near the small ribs; and there is much pain and great suffering and sighing; and all the shoulder limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, by chance some undigested food may spurt from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes in the abdomen, and no sign of it can be found through the intestines, there is no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes to flow, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and rib and thigh and legs, and limbs like these, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for which reason you should act differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell in the skull at the base of the nose: I felt it and pulled it out from the other side under the ear fat, and he was safe without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he drew out an arrow that had struck the fat under his eye below the membrane, and the arrow was embedded, and only the tip towards the shaft could be reached, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all iron without feathers; the youth was safe, and no ill accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with feathers: I seized the barbs, and carefully extracted it as much as possible, and the Christian was safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he drew an arrow from the man who had it embedded in his abdomen, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; I cut around the arrow, probed it, and forcefully extracted it, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow embedded in his back, and the wound is sealed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change his natural disposition, nor causes harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man who has an arrow shot into his face, and the wound is sealed over; and it remains thus without him suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was drawn from the head of the king's prince, which was embedded between his nose, and it was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely bent. I was called for the treatment after it had been embedded for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it thoroughly with a fine probe, and felt nothing; yet he experienced sharp pain and injury inside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I applied a poultice that was both attracting and digesting, so that the area would not swell; and then I saw the site where the arrow had been.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several more days, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose one day; and then he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow that adhered in place; then I added more of this corrosive medicine into the wound opening, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and after about four months, I cut around it so that the wound opened widely enough for me to insert pliers, moving them from one side to another but it would not come out; therefore I did not stop trying various tools until on one day with well-made pliers as described at the end of this chapter, I extracted it and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then closed the wound, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters compare well with great things, and on what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows come out of the limbs where they are embedded in two ways: either from the place where they entered, or from another part; and those that come out from where they entered, are penetrating arrows, and sometimes they come out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out immediately, leave it until the flesh around it is ripe and the exit point is clean; and likewise, if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and gently move it each day; then it will come out, and if it still does not come out, pierce around with a fine needle until the area around it is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it as it is for a few days, because if the arrow reaches the dura mater, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not reach the dura mater, and the patient remains for a few days without any adverse incident, then attempt to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, administer poultices around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is placed in the body so that it cannot be seen, search throughout the tent; and if you feel it, remove it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, cut the skin as wide as necessary for the wound; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, remove the flesh which is embedded on both sides up to where you can reach, and then break or bend the barbs so that you may extract it; and carefully avoid breaking the shaft of the arrow, for this would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one attempt, leave it until the surrounding area is healed, then remove it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood goes against you, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be wary of cutting the nerve and the vein, and place the arrow as you can draw it out without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to how he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then set it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where some sign of it is apparent, or the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or feel it clearly: cut then above it as far as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: do so now without delay.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it and then continue the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push along with all of the shaft; and if the shaft breaks off, and you wish to administer a probe, provide the instrument with a head so that the point of the arrow enters into the tip of the instrument; and then push hard, and if the arrowhead is embedded, insert an instrument with a sharp end to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is touched, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in the thigh or abdomen or bladder or side, and it is close to the surface, then cut into it; but be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the probe for hair is also like the feather of a bird, to insert into the tip of the arrow, as shown here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the pincers for pushing and grasping is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed to become healthy, sixteen of which are in the head: two beating veins behind the ears, called the 'two herbech'; and the two arteries visible in the temples; and the two veins that are in the tear ducts under each eye, called 'aspires'; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose; and the two jugular veins in the neck; and the two veins on the upper lips, which are called 'augeherich'; and the two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which blood is commonly drawn are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and laypeople call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste," and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and laypeople call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and laypeople call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the fossa, and this is the vein from which blood is drawn, which appears clearly on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the savaric vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has II branches; and in the leg and foot are III veins: one is behind the bend of the left wrist, and the second sophene which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nesse," which is on the other ankle; and in the other leg are III veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and headaches; and the qualities of this bloodletting, as I tell you, are that you raise the patient’s head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a bandage so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: pinch them then at your hand, and where you feel the pulse under your fingers, apply pressure there; then take the lancet, and pierce below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein, cut through both skin and vein well twice across, let out as much blood as you wish; then bind it tight until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The application of the two arteries that are in the two temples is suitable for chronic migraine, and severe headache, and customary ophthalmia with continuous tears in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding should be as I say: it is that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; then feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then incise slightly; lift the arm above the vein on top of your finger, and insert the lancet below, and lift the vein up, and cut it as you did in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein for ancient face diseases and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the vein becomes apparent; then take the instrument which is called "the scooper", whose form is here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press firmly with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity you wish; then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is healthy; sometimes work it with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not suitable for the flame to be too sharp; and the vein should run straight, because the bone is close by, and perhaps the flame might break if it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The salve of the two veins that are in the two lacrimal bones helps with the eyes, and for tinea, and for redness, and for cataracts in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their salve is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting some kind of band as before; then apply the salve, and let it be thick, a little longer than flame-shaped, a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bandage it with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The salve of the vein of the nose is useful for fever, and violent fluxes, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the salve is such that the patient strains his neck, then strain his nose with your left hand, take a fine long flame, and place it between the lips in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well inwardly, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, let the blood flow according to your need, then bandage it for one night, because it heals very quickly; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two binders helps in tightening the muscle, and at the beginning of mixing, and with many diseases, and for empetigine, and for corrosives, and herpes, and erythemas; and the qualities of the salve are that the patient tightens his neck under one and the other as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein slightly widely, then draw moderate blood, or as much as is necessary; then treat the other vein similarly, then untie the bandage, and tighten all the veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of the leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The inflammation of the veins above the lips helps against decay of the gums, and splits of the lips, and nose, and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of this inflammation are to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their blackness, and by the small black veins around them: therefore cut each of them, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt, cut the largest on each side, and likewise do for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the inflammation beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The healing of the veins that are below the tongue aids after the healing of the cephalic vein, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the healer are such that the patient urinates between your hands facing the sun, and lifts up the tongue, and looks below on each side for a black vein: heal then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm that are commonly healed are treated according to two methods: by piercing with a broad and sharp blade like a knife, or with a subtle olive-shaped blade as used for cutting; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the small flame is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick, visible blood, and which contain thick, cloudy blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is used to treat fine veins, where there is fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the healer to bleed carefully, and to avoid the artery that is behind.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said; and it should not be cauterized with fire, but cut as previously instructed.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica bone does not appear clearly, then you must extract it and change to another approach; either take some of its flesh away, or open a vein in place of it: it appears clearly; and cut with a knife as previously instructed.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to determine the site of bleeding, then in this case you must extract the arm, touch until you find the pulse; then mark the spot on the bone, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife as previously instructed; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see the area swollen, for it is the artery: avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and fine, know that this is arterial blood: hurry then, and place your finger lengthwise, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which happens many times; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; be cautious, and do not move the patient until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop, and you are forced to act, and no medicine is present, then cut the artery if it is exposed, for its end can be found; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a strip of fig skin, and cut it, then apply one half to the wound tightly until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the application should not be difficult in most cases for the small area of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bandage.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The incision of the vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must take care not to cut too deeply for fear of hitting the nerve that lies beneath, which if inflamed could cause great pain and possibly prevent healing; this nerve can often be seen, but sometimes it cannot be discerned due to its subtlety, in which case you should heal it with an instrument called an aësil; and avoid damaging this nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The incision of the cephalic vein helps to drain blood from the head and also assists the eyes; it should be made by piercing with an olive leaf or a myrtle leaf, as this is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one must choose the most gentle place, and it does no harm if it is necessary to do so the first time, and one may repeat the process; and sometimes the area swells when done for the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the salve is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it should only be done to maintain health and prevent future diseases; and it should be performed in one of the three veins which are suitable: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of repletion appear; and one should bleed on the first or third day, two hours or three days later.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The surgeon who treats diseases has no set hours, but must be available day or night, at all times and in any season; and it is not appropriate to operate on children up until fourteen years old, nor on women carrying a fetus from the fourth month onward.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not operate on the elderly who have surpassed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be operated on, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle enema if there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not attract from the intestines harmful superfluities to the principal members; nor should one operate on those who are too full of meat, or drunk, whether male or female; and do not attempt surgery after colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive intercourse with women, labor, staying up late, fasting, or anything else that weakens the body through actions or substances; then thin out the humors if the patient is fat, using food, drinks, and medicines as needed; then take a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood; and operate on the vein around the third hour of the day, as we have said; and keep yourself free from work, pain, lust, and similar things that day; be cheerful and happy; let the surgeon stand higher than the patient being operated on, and rub the arm two or three times; then loosen the tourniquet moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow properly; then massage the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the lancet with a little old oil; place your left hand on the vein below where you intend to operate so that the vein does not move when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like cords to the surgeon, and some are full of windiness, so when one places the flame on them, it withdraws from the flame, and thus one cannot open the vein, and if one works on the vein, the wound is too narrow; therefore, it is necessary for surgeons to be cautious in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened the first time, it is good; if not, then begin again a little below that place quickly, unless the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will come; nor enter a bath, then restart the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, and you fear that not enough blood will flow as you wish, apply the flame directly to that point rapidly; work a bit quickly, so that the area remains swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a little poultice of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the poultice of oil is soft; and thus administer the poultice of oil each time you bleed the veins to stop the flow of blood; and similarly, when one applies the triacle and bandages, do so gently as the blood may clot if it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when the bleeding is not done forcefully enough or the vein opening is small, hurry and apply a sponge soaked in warm water and salt to the area for one hour; and it must be done after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if some blackness or greenish color remains at the site after several days, it does no harm; and if you wish, place something made of aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance occur at the base of the thumb: place your hand upon it, and if you find the spot soft under the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid placing anything from what we have said above, for it may cut into the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat with another method until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out the blood according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, make a wider wound, and let the flaps be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and this should be done by cutting across, not deep; and this method of bleeding is safe from loss of blood and damage to nerves, and is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body requires bleeding, give him moist bread in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, let him bleed three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat before bleeding moist bread in muscat syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and fragrant syrup, and use other things which we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and faint again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much fainting, that he faints little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to bleed his arm after the first fainting, and he has a strong body, should faint seven hours after the first fainting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to faint from another place, should faint on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw out a large quantity of blood, and widen the vein until it flows freely; then when you heal all conditions for health, place your hand on the pulse as soon as he recovers, so that death does not occur in its place, and this often happens when the healer is negligent. And it should not be done when you wish to loosen the arm and let out blood a second time, and the vein is closed, that you press hard upon it; nor if it is curved, that you stretch the arm quickly, for that would be worse; but leave it until he recovers from bleeding the second time. Or you may touch with the point of flame where the cooled blood at the opening of the vein exits, and place on a little salt mixed in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not bind it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so from the same vein, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the head vein because it is composed appropriately.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient dips their hand in warm water until it turns red; then wrap moderately so that the vein stands out well, then bleed now through it, not across its width or length; and make the incision wide, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not flow, dip the hand again in warm water, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough; and if this is done in summer, do not repeat dipping it in warm water, for it is more often used in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other veins, as there are no artery or nerve near it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salivation of the right hand is effective for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: stretch out the hand, and place it in hot water until the veins swell if they are visible; and if the saliva flows across, and if you cut it entirely through, do not cause any harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are completely bare of flesh underneath, and then put the hand back into hot water if the blood is congealed in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and thread to seal it quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the left hand is effective for the disease of the spleen, and do it exactly as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sinew of the sophene is valuable for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the thighs, and retention of urine, and disease of the knees, and of the old legs and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sinew is that the patient should pour warm water over their foot and rub it on the vein until it softens, and apply it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot there are many veins; heal therefore where the largest vein is, or at the ankle, as this is most effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and heal through them as if cutting; and let the flame be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot in hot water, and let the vein be thoroughly opened.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision fails the first time, start again slightly above it, for the area is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do this equally with the sole of the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its incision relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its incision is such that the patient enters a bath, and applies pressure above the ankle for IV fingers by twisting, because otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, then cut it in all ways you can, including across; it often happens that you must dissect it, as the area is deep, and it responds well to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, take some of the skin from where the heel bone is and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; let the blood flow as much as you wish, then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it; she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping devices are made of horns, wool, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: one by drawing blood, the other without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping that does not involve drawing blood is performed in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and the cupping done by drawing blood and extracting it is performed at fourteen points on the body, of which one is on the top of the head; another is around the neck; two are on each side of the neck; there is a cupping spot under the chin; two spots are on each shoulder; two spots are over the kidneys; two spots are in each arm; two spots are on each leg; and two spots are on each ankle; and this type of cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for that reason it does not weaken a person as when one performs venesection; and it should not be administered either with heat or without heat in any disease caused by excess, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to necessity of illness ventosity is required, or by habit, we bring it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are such people who, when they need to be treated with ventosity, have a heavy head; and there are those who experience bloating and redness in their face, and on their head, neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who see blood drops in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and vomit blood; and there are such people who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially during the middle of the month, we instruct them to undergo ventosity after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The massage of the temple helps with headaches … that come from the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the cephalic massage, and it is not suitable for those who have a cold constitution to use it, or who have catarrh, because it causes them great harm; and therefore it is not appropriate for elderly people to use it, nor for those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who become frequently forgetful should use the cupping glass a bit lower down out of fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventouse on the neck is in place of the head massage and the basilic treatment, and it is useful for tightness in the back, and for fissures in the spinal canal, and for fullness; and this should be applied gently, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause forgetfulness or indigestion or heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosations at the second ribs of the neck is beneficial for headaches, and for ophthalmia and migraine, and for choking, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the health of the basilica; and you must instruct the healer that he should press his hand upon applying, so as not to cut the artery, nor cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventosation below the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, and for gum decay, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is at the place of the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosation of the shoulders is beneficial for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The venous bleeding from the arm is equivalent to that of three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the physician not to cut too deeply, for the area lacks flesh, and there are nerves and arteries beneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup placed on the buttocks is equivalent to hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases below it, and should be large, made of brass, as it needs to pull well; and if it were delicate, it might break; and thus it causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs are very effective, as they draw blood from the entire body, and are beneficial for chronic pains in the thighs, and of the hips, and of the bladder, and reset the flow; and they are placed at the two calves, and at the ankles, and overall they weaken the body after prolonged use, and can cause fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you place it first empty, then temper it slightly, and put it on quickly, moving it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then pierce, and replace the cups, and take care in the condition of the flesh, for there are some who have thin flesh, and clear pores: so one should strike only once, and make large wounds, and somewhat deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the flesh is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to open the way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the flesh is very thick, then it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we only do this once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we bleed much, we often restart it; and if the blood is thick, we pierce deeply, and the ends are such that the wound must be penetrated suddenly, and for those who have thick skin and hard tissue, and whose pores are narrow, you should anoint the areas with suction cups using an appetizing and dissolving oil: if this is in summer, violet oil, or almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if it is autumn, cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, use marjoram oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one to whom treatment is given has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it is necessary to wash after ventosity with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelaine water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have much moisture, they should rise with bath water or water of myrtle and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those who have large excesses, they should rise from old wine, or fig water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar; and it is not appropriate to apply cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after ventosity, and it is necessary for them to exercise, when they should be bled and when they are being bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch if the one who is to be bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; then it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce, and similar things; and eat young birds, and castrated meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and spiced wine that is between old and new, and eat poultry, and young birds and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they will be cupped, they should drink more than they eat; and it is necessary to give some people triacle or nutmeg before cupping or after, to comfort the principal limbs; and their blood should be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink this.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are applied without cutting are those placed on the liver and spleen, for podagra, on the belly and buttocks, and thighs, because these limbs do not bear cutting, except to draw blood from one limb to another as we place them on the breasts when there is a flow of blood; to remove viscosity which is in the limb, just as we apply cupping glasses on the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the swelling; and it removes pain when there is an obstruction or stone, by virtue of its attractive power perhaps removing the obstruction from its place, or dislodging the stone from its location; and similarly it does so when applied to the liver and spleen where there is retained wind, these cupping glasses are administered empty merely to suck up fluid; sometimes they are administered together with heat, and at other times filled with hot water, as in pleurisy diseases, or filling the cupping glass with boiling water alone, or water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two fingers wide and half a palm in depth, and on the side there is one small hole, as if to fit a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of brass or iron to hold a candle with, and they come in different sizes both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for the cupping vessels for children are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.
