Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "humerus," of which one is small, and it is the one that is below the elbow; and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, near the smaller bone. Perhaps only the larger humerus is broken, or the smaller one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the smaller humerus is broken, the restoration and healing are easy; and when the larger one is broken, the healing is difficult, and worse than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small phalanx that is merely broken, then it should be gently stretched out and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large phalanx, then it should be more forcefully compressed; and place him on a cushion, and elevate the poultice of the hand higher than the others, and the small one lower than the other two, and let the patient lie crossed upon himself, with the cushion in front of him raised so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's arm to the underside part of his hand, or at the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the pieces evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are pieces in the fracture, place each one in its place, and if any piece is displaced and pains the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut it out as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the treatment of wounds, I have spoken in a separate chapter; then take that treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration abscesses occur, apply a strip of cerate made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and attach this strip gently, until the hot abscesses are eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate and apply a poultice of powdered miller with plenty of egg; place the strips, and let the strip over the wound be somewhat thicker, and slightly wider than the others; note that there should be six strips on the arm in various positions: whether one or two bones are involved; tighten more around the wound than elsewhere, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths covering the wound be soft and moist, neither hard nor rough; and let the thread used to bind them be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have stated.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and its joint after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident occurs to the limb, such as itching that affects the limb, then it is necessary to rinse the limb with hot water until the itching subsides; and let the limb rest without being too tight.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the compression, and if the joint is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar issues, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And be wary if the swelling cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you should loosen it a bit, and leave it like this for several days until the swelling can move freely, and then compress it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not loosen them until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	When it is around the neck area, then he can place his hands on his neck, and let his necks be even, and beware of movement and displacement, and sleep lying on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few fractures, and it is rare that anything comes but sprains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to sit on a stool and sit straight facing forward evenly; then place his hand on the extended table, and the minister extends the broken bones, and sets them equal, until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, unless abscesses appear, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in one piece of linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the middle of the palm near the base, make a sphere of cloths and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken palm; then wrap it with a long cloth, and place a splint underneath as thick as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is towards the palm, you must place a splint above and another below on the sole, so that the hand remains open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and secure the bandages between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to one of the two bones, which is fractured, place it evenly as required; and secure it with a splint, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in any of the other bones, such as in the index finger or one of the others, place them evenly, and bind them together with the healthy bone that follows; or hold them all together while moving, which may be necessary, or place a splint on it like for a fractured thumb; and take care during restoration and in the disposition of hot abscesses, and support those who come to you as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be seen well when it turns frontward and backward; and the restoration is such that one ligament is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their back, then each assistant extends their ligament equally on their side; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be towards the groin, and the other ligaments below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then the ligament should be near the knee, and the extension downwards; then the physician should set the bone evenly with his two hands, so that it aligns naturally, and then apply the plaster cast, and bind it, unless abscesses appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside then return to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove any excess; then bend the leg so that the heels align with the base of the thigh, and place one long thread between the thigh and the leg beside the knee, with the end of the thread above; then wind the bandage around the leg and thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to ensure equal pressure, then begin to tie tightly three or four turns over the fracture; and as you go further from the fracture, the compression should be less; then tie around the two ends of the thread that were placed between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above it, then retie below at the top of the thread until you reach the foot; tighten it so that it does not move out of place, then leave it as is, so that no abscess or swelling occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, disassemble it and address what comes as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that cause pain, one must remove them if possible; and if not possible, it is necessary to cut the area, and draw out the force; and treat it as we have said, until he is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that splints are placed on it, as with the shoulder and arm; nonetheless, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in forty days, or a few less or a few more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is often fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is usually just a crack, or an opening, and it happens to all wounds, and feels like a wound, and this one can feel very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to place equally those that are flat on both sides until they fit together as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and if necessary, place a round splint, and bind it tightly as needed; then treat all conditions we have mentioned for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar issues; provide each case what is appropriate to it until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by its proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it happens every kind of fracture as it does to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equally as it is for the arm, and the treatment is done accordingly. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg is turned in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the finer bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the larger bone is broken, there is great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and it turns backward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then treat with extension, and place it evenly, and bind the splints equally; but nonetheless, if the fracture is severe and there are many pieces, the extension should be lighter and gentler; and proceed according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two splints that fit the leg from one side and the other, and let them run along the length of the leg from the knee to below; then wrap in two pieces of cloth above and below, and tie it tightly in the middle as well, and at this point the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and thus is well secured; and some apply a poultice along the length of the leg, and if it is made of wood, they place the leg there to prevent movement, and properly done for when there is a break where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the foot bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but in the bones of the foot there sometimes comes a break and at the two toes, and it does not happen that anything fractures except in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot break, and you see these bones protrude one over the other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to go, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, and press them until they return to their places; then apply a plaster and bandages, and place under the bottom of the foot a small board filled with two handfuls, then tighten it to the foot after wrapping with cloths, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, undo the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two are broken, repair them as we have said for the two of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the foot, and it should be slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned, and secure it properly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each one a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and secure the board under the foot; and let them be placed at the top of the board to cover the sole of the foot so that it protects well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said to the other fractures; and treat each case as is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's birth canal is broken, make her sit expanded, then lean her towards the part of the back, and hold her from behind; then fill the woman's birth canal with cotton, and place it in as thickly as the bone; then stand the woman up, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will jump until it reaches the entrance of the birth canal, and return the bone along with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or around that time: the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, tie a tube to the opening, and place the entire bladder inside the birth canal; then blow strongly into the tube until the bladder is inflated within: her birth canal will return to its condition before the fracture; then fill it with cotton again, and leave it that way for some days until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the thumb of a man is broken, or of a woman, restore it as we have said about the thigh bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who applies his study and practice to them, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates in many ways the right way to restore it: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the shaft, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert the shaft into it; then wrap strips around it, and leave it for three days or until it quiets down, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated now, so that the treatments we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then cauterize it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then restart the treatment at the same hour on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscesses are appeased, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the exposed chest, then you must set it gently with your hands, in small increments.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not available to set it evenly with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; for this, a physician must prepare three or four such instruments, as needed for each treatment of fractures; let it be smooth and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it in one motion until it returns to being even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instrument has enough purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either a knife or saw, to your best ability; then remove what remains in the bone of hardness and small pieces.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So place it in its proper place, then moisten the bandage with black styptic wine, and properly if it is a wound; and do not put cerate or anything else on the wound that has oil, for it will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover only around it according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the dressing does not bind with the break; and many times foolish doctors have done this to patients causing death or corrosion in some cases; and let the bindings be looser and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that harm might come as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then splints must not be placed on it; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days swelling at the wound, remove what you have put on entirely wine, and apply healing salve, such as tetrafarmason ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the member twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be prepared in such a way that the swelling runs down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and it cannot heal but swelling returns, know that there are small bone fragments, for which you must probe the wound with a probe, and remove all these displaced pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to that place, or another kind of corruption, then it is necessary for you to treat it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and appears on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar cases involving large limbs, do not attempt to extract it, for many times death results from doing so. Instead, leave it until it becomes rotten; perhaps it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it as is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come upon the joints
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come after the injury to the bruised area, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible sight to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then when the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others; take any of these things or all together and confit them with astringent wine or with an abundance of egg white or with oil; and apply it on the wound in bandages, and press it well, and do not loosen it for several days; then remove it, and start another one until the swelling is gone; or you can press it over a piece of plaster well made; because the property of the plaster is that it removes all swellings from limbs; if the swelling has already turned into hardness such as a stone, and needs to be removed, cut it off above, and let the excess appear on top; or you may remove it with some scraper until it is gone, and treat it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after the recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and the limb remains weak and delicate afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or there were too many bandages, so nutrition could not reach the limb; or due to excessive washing; or from too great movements at the wrong time; or because they lack blood in their body, thus are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and make the body soft, until the blood is multiplied within him; then administer baths, and give joy and rest; then apply pitch to the limb so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and wash frequently with warm water, until the nourishment flows to the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone broken clearly, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those fools who say one should break the limb all over again, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; such work is blamed, and great harms come from it, and perhaps even death; nevertheless, if the joints and the ligaments are fresh, they must be bathed in hot water, or herbs that soften should be cooked, such as leaves of vervain, roots, and hellebore, and similar things; then make a softening plaster as I describe well made, and take the muscilaginous part of vervain, and mix it with fat from hen or oil of cumin, and apply the plaster over it; or take fatty figs and grind them with fine linen flax, and such medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed to rub continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be given to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuous swelling is inflamed and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut down to the bone with a subtle and gentle incision; and apply careful attention and study to the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, it is now necessary to return it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the area swells, and by chance, one may reset it painfully to its place; therefore, it is not advisable to move it when it is swollen: many times this causes spasms and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave him alone until the abscess subsides; then bathe the limb in warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as appropriate according to the treatment's course.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the mandibles are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: where they are slightly removed from their places, and softened a little; or where they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the lower part, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns on its own in many cases.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly, without delay; and in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and pushes his fingers into the root of the dislocated mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other hand should be free to place them evenly; and instruct the patient to soften his mandibles and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the doctor should place it evenly, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if both mandibles are involved, soak them in warm water and oil until you can gently reset them; do not delay in resetting them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth needs to be kept closed and softened, place strips soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax over them, then bind gently with soft linen; let the patient lie on their back, and have their head between two cushions so that it does not move left or right, nor strain to speak, but eat light food until the pain subsides and the mandibles heal; and then eat what they wish lightly, without forcing the mouth open for eating and drinking until the mandible is well healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset properly in an hour, and are not returned to their places, fever and chronic constipation result, and by chance there may be vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then you know it is a prediction of death; and many times the person who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the strength
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The joint cannot be dislocated from the side within the continuity of the rib and the hip, and it is sometimes dislocated outward, which is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is as follows: the patient lies supine on their back and extends their arms; then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the emplastrum and bandage, and secure it; and the head that is towards the side cannot dislocate; if it does, and if it dislocates at any time, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the emplastrum and bandage, and secure it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, the head of the spine is returned when it has been displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is that it dislocates at the side towards the back; and the second is at the lower part; and perhaps upwards, but this rarely happens; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often from below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, because for them it happens quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it occurs with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they suffer a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must then test it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Dislocation is known when it goes down towards the socket, and it makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their difference evident; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and behind the socket touching the top of the shoulder, as if there were an eye; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not concealed, for you will find it clearly by feeling; and this kind of dislocation is not easily reducible when it is new, or if a child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's arm upwards, then places his thumbs under the armpit, and raises the joint forcefully to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then places it underneath; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the minister uses a soothing and softening lotion, such as a decoction of hawthorn, fenugreek, and honey-locust in water, and is applied; then the patient is rubbed on their back, and under the armpit place a pad of wool neither too soft nor too hard, then put your heel under the pad, lift the shoulder powerfully, and pull the arm of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder now returns completely, and if you wish to reset it according to this method: have a person present who is larger than the patient; stand facing the side, place your shoulder under the armpit of the patient, lift the arm upwards, so that the patient hangs on the rope; and another minister pulls the arm of the patient downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, something heavy may be placed with him, and now the dislocation returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another way as follows: one drives a long stake into the ground, which should be about the same thickness as a pistol barrel, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient but cover it with cloths so that the patient does not come into direct contact with it; then extend the patient's arm fully on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return despite all these things we have mentioned, do this treatment: take a stake about two arms' lengths long and four fingers wide, which should be blunt at one end so that it can enter perfectly under the armpit, in this manner:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie over the head of the trunk a cloth to cover it so that the trunk does not hurt the patient, then place it under the seat of the patient; and stretch his arm along the long pole, and tie the shoulder onto the pole, and the hand at the top of the arm, then put the arm on one side of a wide ladder, and let his hands hang down, and let the body dangle from another part: the joint will now heal.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whatever the manner may be, you must put under the seat a pad of even linen, then apply an ointment prepared with powdered mill, with incense and egg yolk, over the entire shoulder and around it, then stretch out under the seat gently, and wrap the bandage over the ointment, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat more after 5 days or 7, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has come to it, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizations with three perforations, as it is described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the hip, and the breasts, or behind, is done by impulse, extension of hands, and treatment at another place; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is stiffness in the limb and slowness in movement, the patient should take many baths until the stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its original condition.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated by bones, and returns to them; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not returned, because one sees it well and feels it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy part, then you can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is displaced, and he cannot bend his arm or touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as if for boil-like swellings, because if they were like boils, it would be difficult to bring back; and perhaps it cannot be fully restored, especially when it is at the rear. It is worse than other dislocations, causes greater pain, and may lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be brought back, you extend his arm with both your hands; and have his arms spread out, and hold his hand around the joint with both of yours, above and below, and push the joint into place at its base or at the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is to the front, it returns when he doubles his hand against his hand, and twists from the base of the palm the knife which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and when two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the joint is at the joint of the hand, apply some oil to soften the joint, then force the joint back into place until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on dry plasters with egg yolk, and press firmly, and bind the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for a few days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, reapply the poultice and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is returned and it moves, bathe and rub gently, and press until it is relieved; or place a sheep's fat pelt on the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it and have him enter the bath; when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the pelt back on, and then have him enter the bath again; do this two or three times until he is healthy; if you wish, place moist birch bark heated with butter on it, and apply it; thus will he return to his condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand occurs, and its reduction is easy, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, before swelling or a hot abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is as follows: you place the injured hand on a table, and the assistant extends the patient's hand, and you position your palm equally above the appearance of the joint, pressing until it returns. Always check if it is in place; then have the patient rest the back of their hand on a board during extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then have the patient place the back of his hand on a table, and you place your hand above the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, then apply soothing plasters to the abscesses and leave them thus without renewing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it and you cannot place it back after several days, then the joint remains dislocated; and it does no harm to the patient as long as the hand is soft, and he cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are severed, or the artery; there is nothing else but to cauterize near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when it is in place, apply the plaster that we have mentioned, then strain it and leave it for five days, then untie it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then apply hot water, and rub it until it is healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated to each side, sometimes at the back or front of the palm; then they are left in place, and the dislocation is pushed back until it returns, then support the head of the finger and move it towards the part where it is dislocated; leave it for two days, and then make it equal on that day; and tie it as we have said, and untie it each day, and move it, and retie it at night; do this often until it is tight, and do exactly the same if it is dislocated in front of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healthy; and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the backsplice
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the dislocation of the back or neck occurs, if there are multiple dislocations, there is no treatment, for death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that vomiting occurs without control, and they cannot hold it, and often some member is weakened, whether both thighs or both arms or one. And often dislocation moves to four parts; the one which moves to the back is called "sciatica": the treatment is that you observe if the sciatica comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing quickly.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients described methods of treatment with grand words, in which there is no great benefit at all; but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding, and have fashioned instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the condition of flatfoot pain in the foot front, there is no remedy; and likewise for the one that comes directly to II sides, and it cannot be treated except properly as I said; and it should be that the patient lie stretched on his face in an equal place, and have a pad under him so he does not hurt himself; then fix a stake at the head in the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a rope beneath the armpits of the patient, and one to the hips, and the knees, and the ankles; and two ministers hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the II stakes; and they should be well fastened, the stake as we have said, and the doctor places his palms on the spine firmly, until it straightens.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board three spans long, and place cloth under the wall, and have the patient lie on their side, then put the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board over the spine; and have the patient place their feet at the other end of the board, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do this in a twisting motion that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And place two torches at the head of the patient from one arm's length apart, and towards the feet another two, with a palm’s distance between each torch both above and below; and in each torch make a hole through which the rope will pass, and secure the torches firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of torches place a rotating torch on which the ropes will turn, and at each turning torch fix two small torches a palm’s length long to turn the main torch; then tie one end of the rope that is around the patient to the turning torch towards the head, and the other end of the rope towards the feet to another turning torch, and each assistant turns their respective torch for the whole body, while the master ensures the spine remains straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equalized, place an absorbent plaster with plenty of egg, and then the bandages, and then a stick three fingers long to cover the area of the protrusion and the part of the healthy spine, then wrap it with linen as we have said, and the patient should be cared for gently until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the stick that we mentioned above; and sometimes a piece of lead is applied, and sometimes an appearance appears in the last vertebra of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but this bone protrudes outwardly, so there should be no presumption about it: perhaps causing death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the hip and at the joints of the shoulder, only dislocations occur, not as with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inward and outward, and front and back; and more often inward than otherwise, and slightly dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of a dislocation inward is that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee appears more bent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the area near it is swollen like an abscess and warm, because the thigh bone ends there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of him who is coming to dislocation are contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who is affected beforehand are that he extends his leg well according to its completion; nevertheless, he does not double it at the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him go forward, he cannot advance, and he retains his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he steps over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is affected from behind are that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in a position below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedy for this type of dislocation is that you observe whether the dislocation is old and remains according to its nature, in which case no treatment is necessary; it should not be forcibly treated.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and this is one of the four types of dislocations, hurry to return the joint, stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and stretch the leg strongly with two hands, or tie a cord above the knee; another assistant places their hand on top in such a way that they push their hands under the patient's armpits, then tighten them with one swift bandage over the thigh; and someone else holds the head of the bandage; and all stretch upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is indeed so.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to treat it accordingly When the dislocation is in the thigh, you must lift the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage at the root of the affected thigh and below the joint; then extend the bandage upward toward the joint and toward the muscle; take another helper's arms and wrap them around the large part of the affected thigh firmly: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot bind it in the manner we have described, then it is necessary to tie the patient's two feet together with a strong bandage below the heels and above the knees, and let the affected leg be extended two palms more than the other; then suspend him by his head from a post, and let him be suspended in the air two arm lengths high; then instruct one helper to embrace the upper part of the thigh, and let other helpers hang with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joint will now return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the case of those with gilbositeit, and bind one cloth properly over the affected leg and another under it; then place two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, and insert a third torch between the patient's thighs in the proper form; and arrange moist cloths around so that they do not burn the patient, then extend each assistant towards him, and the physician should position himself equal to his hand on the dislocation.
